فهمني وقلي هنعمل اي وهل كده عندنا تصور كامل او لا 
**1. Executive Summary**
- The approved business rules are only partially supported today.
- The biggest gaps are: premium is not implemented as one clean generic wallet, add-ons are not category-credit based, delivery is not zone-based, and subscriptions do not have a true immutable contract snapshot.
- The codebase also contains meaningful hidden subscription behavior beyond the approved rules: freeze extension logic, skip-deduct logic, automation fallback, wallet top-ups, custom paid day items, delivery overrides, admin-created subscriptions, and legacy compatibility bridges.

**2. Rule-by-Rule Verification**

**Rule 1. Premium meals**
- Status: Implemented Differently
- Current implementation: There are two premium systems in parallel. Checkout/top-up stores premium wallet rows by exact premiumMealId. Legacy day planning via updateDaySelection deducts premium by count difference on premiumSelections meal IDs. Newer planning via consumePremiumSelection applies a premium upgrade by baseSlotKey + premiumMealId.
- How it differs from the approved rule: This is not one clean generic subscription-level wallet. Extra premium beyond balance is not billed as a paid overage during planning; it is blocked with INSUFFICIENT_PREMIUM. The good news is that no-planning fallback does not auto-consume premium credits.
- Relevant files and functions: [Subscription.js#L64](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Subscription.js#L64), [SubscriptionDay.js#L21](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/SubscriptionDay.js#L21), [subscriptionController.js#L2782](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2782), [subscriptionController.js#L3342](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L3342), [premiumWallet.js#L28](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/utils/premiumWallet.js#L28)

**Rule 2. Add-ons**
- Status: Implemented Differently
- Current implementation: Checkout add-ons are item-based, not category-based. They are stored both as addonBalance wallet rows and as addonSubscriptions recurring subscription add-ons. One-time day add-ons exist through a paid addOneTimeAddon flow, and the webhook adds them to day.addonsOneTime. There is also a separate item-based add-on wallet consumption flow during planning.
- How it differs from the approved rule: There is no category credit wallet for salad/juice/snack. Recurring add-ons are item-based and the recurring representation drops quantity semantics. Type boundaries are weak: checkout/top-up does not strictly prevent one_time add-ons from entering subscription-level flows. Also, updateDaySelection can write addonsOneTime directly, bypassing payment.
- Relevant files and functions: [Addon.js#L19](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Addon.js#L19), [Subscription.js#L66](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Subscription.js#L66), [subscriptionController.js#L911](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L911), [subscriptionController.js#L2915](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2915), [subscriptionController.js#L3592](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L3592), [webhookController.js#L343](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js#L343)

**Rule 3. No-planning fallback**
- Status: Partially Supported
- Current implementation: The automation cutoff job auto-assigns default regular meals when tomorrow’s day is still open and has no selected meals, then locks the day. It carries recurring subscription add-ons in the locked snapshot. It does not auto-consume premium and does not auto-add one-time add-ons.
- How it differs from the approved rule: The fallback exists only in the automation path. Manual locking, kitchen locking, and pickup preparation can lock days without auto-assignment. Automation also filters only by isActive, not availableForSubscription.
- Relevant files and functions: [automationService.js#L26](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/automationService.js#L26), [automationService.js#L43](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/automationService.js#L43), [kitchenController.js#L215](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/kitchenController.js#L215), [subscriptionController.js#L4184](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L4184)

**Rule 4. Delivery and pickup**
- Status: Partially Supported
- Current implementation: Delivery pricing is a flat global setting. Delivery windows are a global settings array. Pickup locations are stored in pickup_locations settings and quote can resolve pickupLocationId. There is pickup preparation logic and delivery records are created when a day moves to out_for_delivery.
- How it differs from the approved rule: There is no zone model, no zone-based pricing, no first-class branch model, and no dynamic slot capacity. “Single branch pickup” is not enforced as a domain rule; the code supports multiple pickup locations via settings.
- Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L960](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L960), [menuController.js#L112](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/menuController.js#L112), [Delivery.js#L3](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Delivery.js#L3), [kitchenController.js#L315](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/kitchenController.js#L315), [settingsController.js#L11](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/settingsController.js#L11)

**Rule 5. Freeze / skip / compensation**
- Status: Implemented Differently
- Current implementation: Freeze is implemented. It marks days as frozen, extends validityEndDate by the number of frozen days, and enforces freezePolicy.maxDays and freezePolicy.maxTimes from the plan. Skip is also implemented, but it deducts meal credits and never creates compensation days. skipRange uses a global skip allowance setting. skipAllowanceCompensatedDays exists on Plan and in the catalog, but I did not find any runtime logic that uses it.
- How it differs from the approved rule: Compensated skip days are not implemented. Skip does not extend the subscription. Freeze compensation exists, but skip compensation does not. Also, freeze policy is read from the current mutable plan, not a stored contract snapshot.
- Relevant files and functions: [Plan.js#L33](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Plan.js#L33), [subscriptionController.js#L1092](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L1092), [subscriptionController.js#L2442](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2442), [subscriptionController.js#L3000](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L3000), [subscriptionService.js#L54](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/subscriptionService.js#L54), [subscriptionCatalog.js#L155](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/utils/subscriptionCatalog.js#L155)

**Rule 6. Subscription contract behavior**
- Status: Implemented Differently
- Current implementation: Paid subscriptions store some checkout-time values such as grams, meals per day, base plan price, delivery choice, and wallet rows. But operational rules still depend on mutable live data like planId.freezePolicy, and plans can be hard-deleted.
- How it differs from the approved rule: There is no full immutable contract snapshot. Existing subscriptions can drift if plans or settings are changed or deleted after payment.
- Relevant files and functions: [Subscription.js#L75](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Subscription.js#L75), [subscriptionController.js#L531](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L531), [adminController.js#L1754](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L1754)

**Rule 7. Admin-editable meal catalog**
- Status: Partially Supported
- Current implementation: Admin can create, update, delete, and toggle regular meals. Menu/catalog endpoints and automation fallback depend on active meal records. Kitchen assignment validates that assigned meals exist and are active.
- How it differs from the approved rule: User day planning does not validate selected meal IDs against the active catalog, so a custom client can still write removed/inactive IDs. Historical and locked snapshots store raw meal IDs, not denormalized meal details, so hard deletion can orphan historical references.
- Relevant files and functions: [mealController.js#L111](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/mealController.js#L111), [mealController.js#L220](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/mealController.js#L220), [subscriptionController.js#L2782](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2782), [automationService.js#L49](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/automationService.js#L49), [SubscriptionDay.js#L94](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/SubscriptionDay.js#L94)

**Rule 8. Old subscriptions**
- Status: Partially Supported
- Current implementation: Old subscriptions remain stored in Subscription and are returned unfiltered in the user subscription list. Canceled and past subscriptions are still visible by ID and in the list endpoint.
- How it differs from the approved rule: I did not find an automatic status-expiry job. Functional expiry is enforced at action time by ensureActive, but the stored status can remain active after validity has passed, which can skew user display and admin reporting.
- Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L1055](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L1055), [subscriptionController.js#L2061](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2061), [adminController.js#L3005](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L3005)

**Rule 9. Hidden subscription logic**
- Status: Supported as an audit task
- Current implementation: The code contains substantial extra subscription logic beyond the approved rules, including automation jobs, top-ups, payment verification, admin create/extend/cancel flows, delivery overrides, custom day purchases, reminder jobs, and legacy compatibility bridges.
- How it differs from the approved rule: The real system is more stateful and more complex than the approved rule list suggests.
- Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L1307](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L1307), [webhookController.js#L45](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js#L45), [automationService.js#L12](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/automationService.js#L12), [notificationSchedulerService.js#L75](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/notificationSchedulerService.js#L75), [adminController.js#L1241](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L1241)

**3. Additional Subscription Logic Found in the Code**
- Optional subscription start date exists. If startDate is omitted, checkout/admin creation defaults to new Date(), which can create a same-day subscription day that user planning APIs cannot edit because planning only allows tomorrow onward. This matters because the first day can become operationally reachable but client-unplannable. Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L1268](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L1268), [subscriptionController.js#L570](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L570), [adminController.js#L1278](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L1278)
- Manual locking paths differ from automation. processDailyCutoff auto-assigns meals before locking, but bulkLockDaysByDate, kitchen transitionDay(..., "locked"), and preparePickup do not. This matters because empty locked days can exist. Relevant files and functions: [automationService.js#L43](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/automationService.js#L43), [kitchenController.js#L215](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/kitchenController.js#L215), [subscriptionController.js#L4184](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L4184)
- Pickup preparation can deduct meal credits and lock a day even when no meals are selected. This matters because pickup-prepared empty days cannot be reopened by kitchen and may have no assignable meal path left. Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L4225](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L4225), [kitchenController.js#L391](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/kitchenController.js#L391)
- There are global and per-day delivery override flows with cutoff protection. This matters because delivery details are mutable after purchase and tomorrow’s effective delivery data is protected only by cutoff logic, not by immutable contract rules. Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L4313](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L4313), [subscriptionController.js#L4379](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L4379)
- Wallet top-up verification exists both via webhook and via user poll/verify endpoints. This matters because payment side effects are protected by payment.applied, but the logic surface is large and duplicated. Relevant files and functions: [subscriptionController.js#L2207](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2207), [subscriptionController.js#L2246](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L2246), [webhookController.js#L225](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js#L225)
- The system supports paid custom salads and custom meals on subscription days. This matters because they affect whether extension days are removable and introduce more day-level paid state than the approved rules mention. Relevant files and functions: [SubscriptionDay.js#L53](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/SubscriptionDay.js#L53), [webhookController.js#L373](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js#L373)
- Reminder automation exists for meal selection, delivery-arriving-soon, and subscription expiry. This matters operationally and also exposes the date-based expiry model. Relevant files and functions: [notificationSchedulerService.js#L21](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/notificationSchedulerService.js#L21), [notificationSchedulerService.js#L75](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/notificationSchedulerService.js#L75), [notificationSchedulerService.js#L123](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/notificationSchedulerService.js#L123)
- Admin can create subscriptions directly, extend them, cancel them, and verify payments manually. This matters because these flows can bypass customer checkout behavior and must be treated as first-class subscription lifecycle logic. Relevant files and functions: [adminController.js#L1241](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L1241), [adminController.js#L3258](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L3258), [adminController.js#L3363](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js#L3363)
- Legacy bridges still exist. premiumRemaining, the legacy premium bucket, legacy skip settings keys, and compatibility alias endpoints are all still active. This matters because migration will have to account for mixed old and new states. Relevant files and functions: [premiumWallet.js#L1](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/utils/premiumWallet.js#L1), [subscriptionService.js#L23](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/subscriptionService.js#L23), [subscriptionController.js#L3848](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js#L3848)

**4. Conflict Map**

**Domain model conflicts**
- Premium is not one generic wallet; it is split between itemized balances, legacy numeric balance, and two planning representations.
- Add-ons are not category-credit based; checkout add-ons become both item wallet rows and recurring live subscription add-ons.
- Subscriptions do not carry a full immutable contract snapshot and still depend on mutable Plan and settings data.
- Plans and meals can be hard-deleted, while active subscriptions and historical days still reference them.

**Pricing conflicts**
- There is no planning-time paid premium overage path; insufficient premium is blocked instead of billed.
- Delivery pricing is flat-setting based, not zone-based.
- Checkout/top-up does not strictly enforce add-on type boundaries, so one-time items can leak into subscription-level purchase state.
- VAT exists globally, but refund/settlement behavior for canceled/expired/unused balances is not implemented as a business flow.

**Planning conflicts**
- User planning does not enforce exact daily meal count; it only blocks over-selection.
- User planning does not validate meal IDs against the active catalog.
- updateDaySelection can directly set addonsOneTime, bypassing payment.
- Manual lock and pickup-prepare paths can create locked days with no meal fallback.

**Operational/dashboard conflicts**
- Kitchen daily orders read recurring subscription add-ons from live subscription.addonSubscriptions, not from the stored locked snapshot, so past operational views can drift.
- Locked and fulfilled snapshots do not denormalize meal names/details, only IDs and some side structures.
- Functional expiry is date-based, but stored subscription status may remain active, which can skew admin dashboards and user displays.
- Kitchen assignment checks premium entitlement count but does not apply the same premium wallet mutation path used by customer planning.

**Delivery/pickup conflicts**
- No zone model, no branch model, no delivery-capacity model.
- Pickup supports multiple setting-based locations rather than a single explicit branch entity.
- Pickup credits are deducted on preparePickup, while delivery credits are deducted on fulfillment.
- Delivery status uses both canceled and cancelled.

**Migration risks**
- Legacy premium bridges and mixed premium day representations are the highest data-model migration risk.
- Existing active subscriptions may be date-expired but not status-expired.
- Hard-deleted plans/meals can already have orphaned references in historical days.
- Recurring add-ons currently depend partly on live subscription data rather than immutable snapshots.

**5. Missing Pieces**
- A true generic premium credit wallet with planning-time paid overage behavior.
- Category-based add-on credits with item choice during planning.
- Zone-based delivery entities and pricing.
- A first-class pickup branch entity, even if there is only one branch for now.
- A full immutable subscription contract snapshot.
- Strong user-side catalog validation for meal planning.
- A clean monetary refund/unused-balance policy and corresponding logic.
- Automatic subscription status expiry/synchronization with validity dates.
- Safe historical denormalization or deletion protections for meals/plans referenced by locked and fulfilled records.

**6. Risk Notes**
- The premium subsystem is the riskiest area because two planning models and legacy bridges coexist.
- updateDaySelection is high risk because it mixes regular selection, legacy premium deduction, and direct one-time add-on writes.
- Payment application is high risk because side effects are spread across webhook, user verify, and admin verify paths.
- Freeze/skip are high risk because business expectations and current logic differ sharply, especially around compensation.
- Historical integrity is high risk because plans and meals can be hard-deleted while snapshots rely heavily on IDs and live references.
- Reporting is high risk because functional expiry and stored status can drift apart.

**7. Final Completeness Assessment**
- Do we now have enough understanding to design a clean phased implementation plan? Yes, mostly. The current behavior is clear enough to design a migration-aware phased plan.
- What business questions are still unresolved, if any? The biggest unresolved questions are: how premium overage should be billed at planning time, exact recurring add-on quantity semantics per day, how to grandfather existing flat-fee delivery subscriptions into zones, what to do with unused balances on cancel/expire, and how to treat already-misclassified legacy add-ons/premium data.
- What code areas must be treated as critical before any refactor? [subscriptionController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js), [webhookController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js), [automationService.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/automationService.js), [kitchenController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/kitchenController.js), [fulfillmentService.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/fulfillmentService.js), [adminController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js), [Subscription.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Subscription.js), [SubscriptionDay.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/SubscriptionDay.js), [Plan.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Plan.js), and [Delivery.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Delivery.js).

أيوه، كده عندنا تصور شبه كامل وقوي جدًا — ليس 100% نهائي، لكن كافٍ جدًا نبدأ منه تخطيط التعديلات بشكل مرتب.

هل نبدأ تعديل الآن؟
ليس تنفيذ مباشر. الخطوة الصحيحة الآن هي تثبيت القرارات الناقصة ثم تصميم Phase 1 فقط.

لو تريد، أكتب لك الآن قائمة القرارات النهائية الناقصة فقط، بشكل نقاط قصيرة جدًا، عشان تحسمها واحدة واحدة.


تب يلا نجاوب علي كل الاسأله الناقصه اكتبها ليا مع شرح واقتراح حل وانا هأكد عليك  وارد علي جميع الاسأله 

تمام.
هجمع لك الآن كل الأسئلة/القرارات الناقصة بشكل مرتب، ومع كل نقطة:

ما معناها

لماذا هي مهمة

اقتراح حل واضح

صيغة قرار جاهزة ترد بها

وأنت بعد ذلك تؤكد كل نقطة أو تعدلها.

1) Premium overage وقت التخطيط
المقصود
لو العميل عنده مثلًا:

3 premium credits
ثم أثناء التخطيط اختار 4 وجبات premium

يبقى استخدم:

3 من رصيده

و1 زيادة

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تحدد:

هل التخطيط يسمح بالزيادة

هل الزيادة تحتاج دفع فوري

هل اليوم يتقفل قبل الدفع أم لا

الاقتراح
أفضل حل عملي:

النظام يسمح باختيار premium أكثر من الرصيد

ويحسب فرق سعر الوجبة premium المختارة

ولا يتم تأكيد هذا اليوم نهائيًا إلا بعد نجاح الدفع الإضافي

القرار المقترح
إذا اختار العميل premium meals أكثر من الرصيد المتاح، يُسمح بذلك فقط عبر paid overage flow، ويتم حساب فرق السعر لكل premium meal إضافية، ولا يتم تثبيت التخطيط النهائي لليوم إلا بعد نجاح الدفع.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

2) هل premium overage يتدفع فورًا أم يتجمع لاحقًا؟
المقصود
لما العميل يختار premium زيادة:
هل:

يدفع فورًا في نفس اللحظة
أم

يتجمع عليه ويحاسب لاحقًا

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تغيّر:

UX

التسعير

المحاسبة

المخاطر المالية

الاقتراح
الأفضل والأكثر أمانًا:

الدفع يكون فوريًا وقت التخطيط

لأن هذا يمنع تراكم مديونية غير مدفوعة

القرار المقترح
أي premium overage يتم سداده فورًا أثناء التخطيط أو قبل تأكيد اليوم، ولا يُسمح بترحيل مبالغ premium الإضافية كرصيد مستحق غير مدفوع.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

3) recurring add-on اليومي: الكمية اليومية
المقصود
لو العميل اشترك في:

سلطة ضمن الاشتراك

هل هذا يعني:

سلطة واحدة يوميًا
أم أكثر؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على:

التسعير

التخطيط

التنفيذ اليومي

شكل البيانات

الاقتراح
اعتماد أبسط وأوضح قاعدة:

كل recurring add-on اشتراكي = وحدة واحدة يوميًا من نفس الفئة

مثال:

daily salad = 1 salad per day

القرار المقترح
إذا اشترى العميل recurring subscription add-on مثل salad، فإنه يحصل على entitlement يومي يتيح له اختيار عنصر واحد فقط من هذه الفئة لكل يوم من أيام الاشتراك.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

4) هل يمكن شراء أكثر من recurring add-on من نفس الفئة؟
المقصود
هل العميل يمكنه شراء:

2 سلطة يوميًا طوال الاشتراك؟
أم فقط واحدة؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تحدد:

هل الحقل boolean أم quantity

وكيف نحسب السعر

وكيف ينفذ المطعم

الاقتراح
لو تريد تبسيط الإصدار الأول:

اسمح فقط بوحدة واحدة يومية لكل فئة

ثم لاحقًا يمكن توسيعها

القرار المقترح
في الإصدار الحالي، recurring subscription add-ons تُدعم بحد أقصى عنصر يومي واحد لكل فئة (مثل سلطة واحدة يوميًا، عصير واحد يوميًا، سناك واحد يوميًا)، وأي زيادة مستقبلية تعتبر enhancement لاحقًا.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

5) one-time add-ons: هل تُدفع فورًا؟
المقصود
لو العميل أثناء التخطيط اختار:

عصير لهذا اليوم فقط

أو سلطة إضافية لهذا اليوم فقط

هل يجب أن يدفع فورًا؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تحدد:

هل اليوم يمكن يتثبت بدون دفع

وهل فيه التزام مالي معلق

الاقتراح
الأفضل:

أي one-time add-on مدفوع يجب سداده فورًا قبل تثبيت اليوم

القرار المقترح
أي one-time day add-on يتم شراؤه أثناء التخطيط يجب سداده قبل تأكيد تخطيط اليوم، ولا يجوز إضافته إلى اليوم بشكل نهائي بدون payment success.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

6) لو العميل لم يخطط: recurring add-on كيف يُنفذ؟
المقصود
أنت ثبت بالفعل أن:

لو عنده سلطة يومية

ولم يخطط

يجب أن تخرج له السلطة

لكن بقي سؤال:
هل النظام يختار له عنصرًا افتراضيًا من هذه الفئة؟
أم المطعم يختار يدويًا؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على الـ auto-assignment

الاقتراح
أفضل حل الآن:

النظام أو فريق التشغيل يختار عنصرًا regular/default متاحًا من نفس الفئة حسب availability

القرار المقترح
إذا لم يخطط العميل يومه قبل cutoff وكان لديه recurring add-on يومي، يتم تعيين عنصر افتراضي متاح من نفس الفئة بواسطة النظام أو فريق التشغيل، ويعتبر ذلك fulfillment صحيحًا لهذا الـ recurring add-on لذلك اليوم.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

7) auto-assignment للوجبات الأساسية: هل دائمًا regular فقط؟
المقصود
لو العميل لم يخطط:
هل النظام يختار له:

regular meals فقط

بدون premium نهائيًا

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على الرصيد والتشغيل

الاقتراح
نعم، الأفضل:

auto-assignment = regular only

لا premium تلقائي

القرار المقترح
عند no-planning fallback، يتم تعيين regular meals فقط تلقائيًا، ولا يتم اختيار premium meals تلقائيًا تحت أي ظرف في الإصدار الحالي.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

8) exact meal count per day
المقصود
لو الخطة 3 وجبات يوميًا:
هل لازم كل يوم يكون فيه بالضبط 3 وجبات؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تضبط:

التخطيط

المطبخ

التسليم

الـ fallback

الاقتراح
نعم، لازم exactly mealsPerDay

القرار المقترح
كل يوم من أيام الاشتراك يجب أن يحتوي على exactly mealsPerDay من الوجبات الأساسية، سواء اختارها العميل بنفسه أو تم auto-assignment من النظام بعد cutoff.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

9) start date الافتراضي
المقصود
الكود الحالي قد يبدأ الاشتراك اليوم لو لم يرسل startDate

وده قد يخلق يومًا أول غير قابل للتخطيط للمستخدم

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تسبب edge case تشغيلية

الاقتراح
الأفضل:

startDate الافتراضي يكون غدًا

وليس اليوم
إلا إذا الأدمن أنشأ اشتراكًا خاصًا يدويًا

القرار المقترح
إذا لم يحدد العميل startDate أثناء الشراء، يكون startDate الافتراضي هو اليوم التالي، وليس نفس اليوم، لتجنب إنشاء يوم تشغيلي غير قابل للتخطيط من المستخدم.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

10) الاشتراكات القديمة: grandfathering أم migration؟
المقصود
عند نقل النظام الجديد:
هل الاشتراكات القديمة:

تظل على المنطق القديم
أم

تتحول للموديل الجديد

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على:

المخاطر

الجهد

الدعم الفني

سلامة البيانات

الاقتراح
الأكثر أمانًا:

الاشتراكات الحالية النشطة تُعامل كـ grandfathered

والجديد فقط يدخل على الموديل الجديد

إلا لو في migration واضحة وآمنة

القرار المقترح
الاشتراكات الحالية النشطة تُحافظ على سلوكها القائم كـ grandfathered subscriptions ما أمكن، بينما الاشتراكات الجديدة فقط تُنشأ على target model الجديد، إلا إذا تم اعتماد migration صريحة وآمنة لبعض العناصر المحددة.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

11) unused premium credits عند انتهاء الاشتراك
المقصود
لو العميل اشترى 3 premium credits واستخدم 2 فقط، وبقي 1 حتى نهاية الاشتراك

ما الذي يحدث؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على:

الدعم

النزاعات

المحاسبة

الاقتراح
أبسط سياسة تشغيلية:

تنتهي بانتهاء الاشتراك

لا refund

لا rollover
إلا إذا عندكم سياسة تجارية مختلفة

القرار المقترح
أي premium credits غير مستخدمة تنتهي بانتهاء صلاحية الاشتراك، ولا تُرحّل ولا تُرد ماليًا في الإصدار الحالي ما لم توجد سياسة استثنائية معتمدة.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

12) unused recurring add-ons عند عدم الاستخدام
المقصود
لو العميل عنده:

سلطة يومية
لكن لم يخطط
أو النظام اختار تلقائيًا
أو لم يستلم

هل تعتبر مستهلكة؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأن recurring add-on اليومي ليس wallet عادي، بل حق يومي ضمن الاشتراك

الاقتراح
طالما اليوم دخل في fulfillment:

recurring add-on لذلك اليوم يعتبر مستحق التنفيذ ضمن اليوم

ولا يترحل لليوم التالي

القرار المقترح
Recurring subscription add-ons هي entitlements يومية مرتبطة بكل يوم من أيام الاشتراك، ولا يتم ترحيل entitlement يوم غير مستخدم إلى يوم لاحق، ما لم توجد قاعدة استثنائية صريحة مثل freeze أو skip مع تعويض.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

13) unused one-time add-ons لو فشل اليوم أو اتلغى
المقصود
لو العميل دفع one-time add-on لهذا اليوم، ثم اليوم اتلغى أو تجمّد أو تغيّر

ماذا يحدث؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على settlement / refund

الاقتراح
أقرب حل منطقي:

إذا اليوم لم يُنفذ أصلًا بسبب freeze/skip قبل التحضير:

one-time add-on يرجع كرصيد أو refund pending

أما إذا دخل التنفيذ فلا يرجع

القرار المقترح
إذا تم شراء one-time add-on ليوم معين ثم أُلغي هذا اليوم أو جُمّد قبل بدء التحضير/التنفيذ، يجب إرجاع قيمته كرصيد أو رد مالي حسب سياسة الدفع المعتمدة. أما بعد بدء التنفيذ فلا يحق استرداده تلقائيًا.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

14) skip compensation
المقصود
أنت كنت تتوقع أن:

بعض الخطط تسمح بعدد skip days مع تعويض
لكن الكود الحالي لا يطبق ذلك فعلًا

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأننا لازم نحسم:

هل نريد هذه الميزة فعلاً في target model؟
أم نؤجلها؟

الاقتراح
لو هي جزء مهم من البزنس عندك:

اعتمدها رسميًا في target model

لكن كمرحلة لاحقة بعد تثبيت الأساس

القرار المقترح
Compensated skip days are an approved target business rule and must be implemented in the new model, but they may be scheduled after core contract, premium, add-on, and planning corrections are stabilized.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

15) الفرق بين freeze و skip
المقصود
هل تريد بوضوح أن:

freeze = يوقف الأيام ويزيد end date

skip = يتجاوز اليوم وقد يحصل تعويض ضمن limit

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأن الكود الحالي يخلط النتائج جزئيًا

الاقتراح
نعم، لازم التمييز يكون صريح

القرار المقترح
Freeze and skip are separate business actions. Freeze pauses subscription days and extends validity according to freeze policy. Skip marks specific days as skipped and may extend validity only within the compensated skip policy defined by the subscription contract.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

16) delivery migration إلى zones
المقصود
عندك اشتراكات قديمة flat-fee، والنظام الجديد سيكون zone-based

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على العدالة والفواتير والنزاعات

الاقتراح
الأأمن:

الاشتراكات القديمة تستمر على منطقها القديم

الجديدة فقط تدخل zone-based

ثم later migration if needed

القرار المقترح
Existing delivery subscriptions created before zone-based rollout should remain grandfathered on their original delivery pricing/logic unless an explicit migration communication and re-pricing policy is approved.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

17) single branch pickup
المقصود
هل نثبت الآن أن pickup branch واحد فقط في الإصدار الحالي؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على الموديل والـ admin

الاقتراح
نعم، branch واحد الآن، مع قابلية توسعة لاحقًا

القرار المقترح
The current target model assumes a single active pickup branch in this release. The model may remain extensible for future multi-branch support, but current business behavior is single-branch only.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

18) صلاحية تعديل catalog على الأيام القديمة
المقصود
هل حذف/تعطيل meal من الداشبورد يجب أن يؤثر على الأيام القديمة المقفولة؟

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأن التاريخ والتقارير والمطبخ يعتمدون عليها

الاقتراح
لا، التغيير يجب أن يؤثر على المستقبل فقط

القرار المقترح
Admin catalog changes affect future planning and future auto-assignment only. Historical, locked, and fulfilled days must preserve their recorded items and remain readable even if catalog items are later disabled or removed.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

19) status expiry للاشتراكات
المقصود
الكود الحالي قد يترك الاشتراك active في الداتا حتى بعد انتهاء المدة فعليًا

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأنها تؤثر على profile والتقارير

الاقتراح
لازم يكون عندك:

functional expiry

وstored status sync واضح

القرار المقترح
Subscription stored status must be synchronized with actual validity lifecycle so that expired subscriptions are visibly inactive in user/admin views, while still remaining historically accessible.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

20) admin-created subscriptions
المقصود
الأدمن يقدر ينشئ اشتراك يدويًا

لماذا هذه النقطة مهمة
لأن أي target model لازم يشمل هذا المسار أيضًا، وليس checkout العميل فقط

الاقتراح
نعم، admin-created subscription يجب أن يمر بنفس contract model مع صلاحيات إضافية

القرار المقترح
Admin-created subscriptions must use the same canonical subscription contract model as customer-created subscriptions, with explicit admin-only overrides where needed, rather than bypassing contract consistency.

ردك المطلوب
موافق

أو عدله

الأفضل الآن
رد عليّ بنفس الترتيب، مثلًا:

1 موافق

وأنا بعدها سأحوّل كل القرارات التي توافق عليها إلى وثيقة قرارات نهائية جاهزة نستخدمها مع الـ AI والخطة القادمة.


1. أفضل حل عملي:

النظام يسمح باختيار premium أكثر من الرصيد

ويحسب فرق سعر الوجبة premium المختارة

ولا يتم تأكيد هذا اليوم نهائيًا إلا بعد نجاح الدفع الإضافي

2. الأفضل والأكثر أمانًا:

الدفع يكون فوريًا وقت التخطيط

لأن هذا يمنع تراكم مديونية غير مدفوعة

ممتاز. كده ثبتنا تقريبًا كل القرارات المهمة، وبقينا قريبين جدًا من الـ target business model النهائي.

سأرتب لك الآن النتيجة بشكل واضح:

ما الذي تم اعتماده الآن
1) Premium overage
تم اعتماد الآتي:

النظام يسمح للعميل باختيار premium meals أكثر من الرصيد المتاح

يتم حساب فرق سعر الوجبة premium المختارة

لا يتم تأكيد اليوم نهائيًا إلا بعد نجاح الدفع الإضافي

2) توقيت دفع premium overage
تم اعتماد الآتي:

الدفع يكون فوريًا وقت التخطيط

لا يوجد مديونية معلقة أو تحصيل لاحق

3) recurring add-on اليومي
تم اعتماد:

إذا اشترى العميل recurring add-on مثل salad

يحصل على عنصر واحد يوميًا من هذه الفئة

4) حد recurring add-on لكل فئة
تم اعتماد:

في الإصدار الحالي: حد أقصى عنصر يومي واحد لكل فئة

مثل:

سلطة واحدة يوميًا

عصير واحد يوميًا

سناك واحد يوميًا

5) one-time add-ons
تم اعتماد:

أي one-time day add-on يتم شراؤه أثناء التخطيط

يجب سداده قبل تأكيد اليوم

6) recurring add-on في حالة no-planning
تم اعتماد:

إذا لم يخطط العميل يومه

وكان لديه recurring add-on يومي

يتم اختيار عنصر افتراضي متاح من نفس الفئة بواسطة النظام أو فريق التشغيل

7) auto-assignment للوجبات الأساسية
تم اعتماد:

auto-assignment يكون regular meals فقط

لا يتم اختيار premium تلقائيًا

8) exact meals per day
تم اعتماد:

كل يوم يجب أن يحتوي على exactly mealsPerDay

سواء اختاره العميل أو تم auto-assignment

9) start date الافتراضي
تم اعتماد:

إذا لم يحدد العميل startDate

يكون الافتراضي هو اليوم التالي

وليس نفس اليوم

10) الاشتراكات القديمة + التجديد
تم اعتماد:

الاشتراكات الحالية النشطة تبقى grandfathered قدر الإمكان

والاشتراكات الجديدة فقط تدخل على الموديل الجديد

وتمت إضافة قرار مهم:

قرار إضافي معتمد
يقدر اليوزر يجدد الاشتراك على نفس الباقة القديمة مباشرة

طالما الباقة ما زالت متاحة

بدون الحاجة أن يعيد الاختيار من البداية كل مرة

وده قرار ممتاز ومهم جدًا للـ UX.

11) unused premium credits
تم اعتماد:

أي premium credits غير مستخدمة

تنتهي بانتهاء الاشتراك

لا rollover

لا refund تلقائي

12) unused recurring add-ons
تم اعتماد:

recurring add-ons هي entitlement يومي

لو يوم انتهى، لا تنتقل entitlement إلى يوم آخر

إلا في حالات استثنائية مثل freeze/skip المعوض حسب القواعد

13) one-time add-ons إذا أُلغي اليوم أو جُمّد
أنت قلت:

في هذه المرحلة غير متأكد تمامًا

لكن “اعملها كده”

إذن هذه النقطة سنعتبرها قرارًا مؤقتًا معتمدًا كالتالي:

القرار المؤقت
إذا تم شراء one-time add-on ليوم معين

ثم أُلغي اليوم أو جُمّد قبل بدء التحضير/التنفيذ

يتم إرجاعه كرصيد أو رد مالي حسب سياسة الدفع

أما بعد بدء التنفيذ فلا يُسترد تلقائيًا

هذه النقطة تحتاج لاحقًا مراجعة تشغيلية/محاسبية أدق، لكن حاليًا عندنا اتجاه واضح.

14) compensated skip days
تم اعتماد:

compensated skip days جزء من target model

لكن يمكن جدولتها بعد تثبيت الأساس

15) الفرق بين freeze و skip
تم اعتماد:

Freeze و Skip عمليتان مختلفتان

Freeze يوقف الأيام ويمدد الصلاحية حسب policy

Skip قد يمدد فقط ضمن compensated skip policy

16) delivery migration
تم اعتماد:

الاشتراكات القديمة الخاصة بالتوصيل تبقى على منطقها القديم قدر الإمكان

الجديدة فقط تدخل zone-based

إلا إذا وُجدت migration policy صريحة لاحقًا

17) single branch pickup
تم اعتماد:

الإصدار الحالي مبني على فرع استلام واحد فقط

مع قابلية توسعة مستقبلية

18) تأثير تعديل catalog
تم اعتماد:

تعديل الأدمن على catalog يؤثر على المستقبل فقط

الأيام القديمة / locked / fulfilled يجب أن تبقى محفوظة وقابلة للقراءة

19) status expiry
تم اعتماد:

حالة الاشتراك في الداتا يجب أن تكون متزامنة مع الصلاحية الفعلية

بحيث الاشتراك المنتهي يظهر inactive بوضوح

مع بقائه ظاهرًا تاريخيًا

20) admin-created subscriptions
تم اعتماد:

اشتراكات الأدمن يجب أن تستخدم نفس canonical contract model

مع صلاحيات admin-only overrides عند الحاجة

وليس bypass كامل للنظام

Final Approved Business Decisions
Subscription System Target Model
This document defines the final approved business rules for the subscription system.
These rules are the source of truth for the backend architecture and future implementation phases.

No implementation should contradict the decisions defined here.

1. Premium Meals Model
1.1 Premium Wallet
Premium meals are implemented as a generic subscription-level credit wallet.

Example:

User purchases:

3 premium meals

System stores:

premiumCreditsPurchased = 3
premiumCreditsRemaining = 3
During meal planning:

Selecting a premium meal consumes 1 premium credit.

1.2 Premium Overage
Users are allowed to select more premium meals than their remaining premium credits.

Example:

User has:

premiumCreditsRemaining = 2
User selects:

3 premium meals
Result:

2 meals consume existing credits

1 meal becomes premium overage

1.3 Premium Overage Payment
Premium overage must be paid immediately during planning.

Rules:

The system calculates the price difference of the selected premium meal

The day planning cannot be confirmed until payment succeeds

No unpaid premium overage is allowed

1.4 No Automatic Premium Consumption
Premium credits must never be consumed automatically by the system.

If the user does not plan their meals before cutoff:

The system may auto-assign regular meals only

Premium credits remain untouched.

2. Add-On System
The system supports two types of add-ons.

2.1 Recurring Subscription Add-Ons
Recurring add-ons are daily entitlements included in the subscription.

Example:

User purchases:

Daily Salad
This gives:

1 salad entitlement per subscription day
2.2 Recurring Add-On Quantity
In the current release:

Each recurring add-on category is limited to:

1 item per day
Examples:

Daily Salad → 1 salad per day
Daily Juice → 1 juice per day
Daily Snack → 1 snack per day
Future versions may allow higher quantities.

2.3 Recurring Add-On Behavior if User Does Not Plan
If the user does not plan meals before cutoff:

The system auto-assigns regular meals

Recurring add-ons must still be fulfilled

The system or restaurant may select a default available item from that category.

Example:

User has:

Daily Salad
If the user did not select the specific salad:

The system may assign:

Caesar Salad
or
Greek Salad
based on availability.

2.4 One-Time Add-Ons
Users may purchase one-time add-ons during meal planning.

Examples:

Add juice for today
Add extra salad for today
Add snack for today
These apply only to a specific day.

2.5 One-Time Add-On Payment
One-time add-ons must be paid before the day plan is confirmed.

Rules:

No unpaid one-time add-ons

No automatic one-time add-ons by the system

3. Meal Planning Rules
3.1 Exact Meal Count Per Day
Each day must contain exactly:

mealsPerDay
Example:

Plan = 3 meals per day
Each day must contain exactly:

3 meals
This rule applies to:

user planning

auto-assignment fallback

3.2 No Planning Fallback
If the user does not plan meals before cutoff:

The system may automatically assign:

regular meals only
Rules:

premium meals are never auto-assigned

recurring add-ons are still fulfilled

4. Subscription Start Date
If the user does not provide a start date during checkout:

The system must set:

startDate = tomorrow
This prevents creating a same-day operational day that the user cannot plan.

5. Subscription Renewal
Users may renew their subscription directly from their previous subscription if the plan is still available.

Example:

User has:

10 day plan
After expiry:

User may choose:

Renew this plan
without repeating the full configuration process.

6. Old Subscriptions (Grandfathering)
Existing active subscriptions should remain grandfathered as much as possible.

Meaning:

They continue using the logic that existed when they were created

New subscriptions use the new target model

Migration may occur later if explicitly planned.

7. Unused Premium Credits
Unused premium credits expire with the subscription.

Rules:

No rollover
No refund
No transfer
Unless a future policy explicitly introduces it.

8. Recurring Add-On Expiry
Recurring add-ons are daily entitlements.

If a day passes:

The entitlement for that day is consumed or expired

It does not carry forward to another day

Exception:

freeze

compensated skip

if applicable.

9. One-Time Add-On Refund Policy
If a one-time add-on was purchased for a day and:

the day is frozen

the day is skipped

the day is cancelled

before preparation begins:

The add-on should be:

refunded
or
returned as balance
depending on the payment policy.

If preparation has already started:

no automatic refund
10. Freeze vs Skip
Freeze and skip are separate actions.

Freeze
Freeze:

pauses subscription days

extends subscription validity

follows freeze policy defined by the plan

Skip
Skip:

marks a specific day as skipped

may extend validity within compensated skip policy limits

11. Compensated Skip Days
Compensated skip days are an approved business rule.

However:

Implementation may be scheduled after core system stabilization.

12. Delivery Model
Current system will migrate to zone-based delivery.

However:

Existing subscriptions using flat delivery pricing should remain grandfathered.

New subscriptions use the zone model.

13. Pickup Model
Current release assumes:

Single pickup branch
The system architecture may remain extensible for future multi-branch support.

14. Catalog Changes
Admin changes to meals or add-ons affect:

future planning only
Historical data must remain intact.

Locked or fulfilled days must still show their original data even if the catalog item was removed.

15. Subscription Status Expiry
Subscription status must reflect real validity.

Expired subscriptions should:

be marked inactive
but remain visible for historical access.

16. Admin-Created Subscriptions
Admin-created subscriptions must use the same canonical contract model as customer-created subscriptions.

Admin may have additional override capabilities but should not bypass contract consistency.

17. Operational Fallback Rules
Operational automation must respect:

exact meal counts

recurring add-ons

premium wallet rules

cutoff timing

No automation path should violate entitlement accounting.

Final Note
This document defines the approved target model for the subscription system.

All future backend changes must align with this model.

Implementation should proceed using a phased migration plan, beginning with contract stabilization and payment consistency.

لو حابب، الخطوة التالية اللي أنصح بها هي:
أكتب لك Prompt أقوى جدًا للـ AI الآن يجعله:

2️⃣ يحدد ما الذي يجب تغييره في كل Phase بدقة
3️⃣ ويصمم Phase 1 فقط بشكل تقني عميق قبل أي تعديل في الكود.

Your task now is NOT to implement code yet.

IMPORTANT RULES

- Do NOT change schema yet.
- Do NOT refactor controllers yet.
- Do NOT move to Phase 2 implementation.
- First update the plan, then produce Phase 1 technical design only.
- If you find any conflict between the approved business decisions and the current codebase, explicitly point it out.
- Keep migration safety in mind at all times because the current codebase has legacy bridges and mixed models.

APPROVED BUSINESS DECISIONS

1. Premium meals are a generic subscription-level credit wallet.
2. Selecting a premium meal during planning consumes 1 premium credit.
3. Users may select premium meals beyond their remaining balance, but this becomes a paid premium overage flow.
4. Premium overage must be paid immediately during planning before the day can be confirmed.
5. Premium credits must never be consumed automatically by fallback or automation.
6. Recurring subscription add-ons are daily entitlements included in the subscription.
7. In the current release, recurring add-ons are limited to one item per category per day.
8. If the user has a recurring add-on such as daily salad, it must still be fulfilled even if the user does not plan that day.
9. If the user does not plan a day before cutoff, the system may auto-assign regular meals only.
10. Auto-assignment must still include recurring daily add-ons.
11. One-time add-ons are day-level paid add-ons purchased during planning for a specific day only.
12. One-time add-ons must be paid before the day plan is confirmed.
13. Each day must contain exactly mealsPerDay base meals.
14. Default subscription start date should be tomorrow if the user does not provide one.
15. Users may renew the same previous subscription plan directly if that plan is still available.
16. Existing active subscriptions should remain grandfathered as much as possible.
17. Unused premium credits expire with the subscription.
18. Recurring add-ons are daily entitlements and do not roll forward to later days.
19. One-time add-ons should be refundable or returned as balance only if the day is cancelled/frozen/skipped before preparation starts.
20. Freeze and skip are separate actions.
21. Compensated skip days are an approved target business rule, even if implemented later than the core phases.
22. Delivery must move to a zone-based model for new subscriptions.
23. Existing delivery subscriptions should remain grandfathered unless an explicit migration policy is approved.
24. Pickup is single-branch in the current release.
25. Catalog changes affect future planning only; locked and fulfilled historical records must remain readable and preserved.
26. Subscription status must reflect real validity and expired subscriptions should appear inactive while remaining historically visible.
27. Admin-created subscriptions must use the same canonical contract model as customer-created subscriptions, with explicit admin-only overrides if needed.
28. Operational automation must respect exact meal counts, recurring add-ons, premium wallet rules, and cutoff timing.

اي الخطوه التاليه 
**1. Revised phased implementation plan**

Direct conflicts between the approved business decisions and the current codebase that drive this revised plan:
- Premium overage is currently blocked, not converted into an immediate paid planning flow.
- Premium is still stored and consumed through mixed itemized and legacy mechanisms, not one clean generic wallet.
- Add-ons are still item-based at checkout/top-up, not recurring daily category entitlements plus paid day-level one-time add-ons.
- updateDaySelection can still write one-time add-ons directly onto a day without payment.
- No-planning fallback exists only in automation and is not consistently enforced across all lock paths.
- The default subscription start date still falls back to “today”, not “tomorrow”.
- Customer checkout and admin-created subscriptions do not converge on one canonical contract model.
- Webhook verification and manual verification still duplicate payment-application logic.
- Delivery is still flat-fee/settings-based, not zone-based.
- Subscription status can functionally expire without the stored status becoming inactive.
- Existing subscriptions are not clearly bounded as grandfathered contract types.

**Phase 1 — Canonical Contract, Payment Consistency, and Renewal Foundation**
- Classification: must-do for correctness
- Objective: make every new subscription originate from one canonical contract snapshot, with consistent payment application, idempotency, tomorrow-default start date, admin/customer alignment, and renewal support.
- Why this phase is needed: the current system has no full immutable contract snapshot, duplicated activation logic, partial idempotency, and different creation rules between customer checkout and admin creation.
- Affected models: CheckoutDraft, Subscription, Payment
- Affected APIs: customer quote/checkout/verify/status, admin create subscription, admin/manual payment verify, renewal initiation API
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, webhookController, adminController
- Migration considerations: old subscriptions remain legacy/grandfathered; new snapshots are additive; partial backfill is allowed but must be explicitly marked as derived/incomplete
- Backward compatibility concerns: legacy subscriptions without snapshots must continue to work through the current read path until later phases
- Operational/dashboard impact: support and admin gain a stable purchased-contract view instead of reconstructing from live plan/settings
- Risks: double-application during cutover, partial backfills, renewal on deleted plans, mismatch between snapshot and legacy runtime fields
- Dependencies: none

**Phase 2 — Canonical Day Planning Core and Historical Preservation**
- Classification: must-do for correctness
- Objective: establish one authoritative day-planning contract with exact mealsPerDay enforcement, no bypass writes, stable lock rules, and preserved historical readability.
- Why this phase is needed: current planning is split across legacy and newer flows, exact meal counts are not enforced, and historical records rely too heavily on mutable references.
- Affected models: SubscriptionDay, Subscription
- Affected APIs: day selection, day retrieval, today/days listing, kitchen assignment inputs
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, kitchenController, automationService, fulfillmentService
- Migration considerations: open future days can be normalized; locked and fulfilled records must remain readable and must not be rewritten destructively
- Backward compatibility concerns: existing mobile/web clients may still send legacy day payloads during the compatibility window
- Operational/dashboard impact: kitchen, automation, and support all read the same day shape and the same lock assumptions
- Risks: this phase touches the highest-traffic behavioral surface in the product
- Dependencies: Phase 1

**Phase 3 — Premium Generic Wallet and Immediate Paid Overage**
- Classification: must-do for correctness
- Objective: replace mixed premium behavior with one generic subscription-level wallet plus immediate paid overage during planning.
- Why this phase is needed: the approved model now requires generic premium credits, paid overage before confirmation, and zero automatic premium consumption in fallback.
- Affected models: Subscription, SubscriptionDay, Payment
- Affected APIs: subscription checkout, premium top-up, day planning, premium selection/removal, future premium-overage payment initiation and verification
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, webhookController, automationService, kitchenController
- Migration considerations: existing premium itemized balances must be aggregated conservatively into grandfathered premium balances; already-consumed legacy rows must remain auditable
- Backward compatibility concerns: legacy subscriptions may continue using legacy premium behavior temporarily if snapshot/grandfather mode marks them as old-contract
- Operational/dashboard impact: wallet reporting simplifies, and kitchen sees premium choices without needing to infer entitlement math manually
- Risks: the current code has the most hidden complexity here; premium migration errors would affect billing and fulfillment
- Dependencies: Phases 1 and 2

**Phase 4 — Recurring Add-On Entitlements, One-Time Add-Ons, and Fallback Alignment**
- Classification: must-do for correctness
- Objective: separate recurring daily add-on entitlements from paid one-time day add-ons, and make fallback automation honor the approved rules.
- Why this phase is needed: the approved model now clearly distinguishes recurring included add-ons from one-time paid day add-ons, while the current code mixes item balances, recurring subscription add-ons, and direct day writes.
- Affected models: Subscription, SubscriptionDay, Addon, Payment
- Affected APIs: checkout, add-on top-up or purchase flows, day planning, one-time day add-on payment initiation/verification, day detail
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, webhookController, automationService, kitchenController
- Migration considerations: existing recurring add-ons must be mapped into daily entitlement form; one-time day add-ons already attached to future days must be preserved as paid historical/day state
- Backward compatibility concerns: current itemized add-on balances may need grandfathered read support before full cutover
- Operational/dashboard impact: fallback can include recurring add-ons reliably; kitchen stops depending on live subscription add-on arrays alone
- Risks: category mapping and grandfather handling are easy to get wrong; this phase also changes automation and planning confirmation boundaries
- Dependencies: Phases 1, 2, and 3

**Phase 5 — Zone-Based Delivery, Single-Branch Pickup Contract, and Real Validity Status**
- Classification: must-do for correctness
- Objective: introduce zone-based delivery for new subscriptions, formalize single-branch pickup, and ensure inactive/expired status reflects real validity while keeping history visible.
- Why this phase is needed: delivery is still flat/settings-based, pickup is setting-driven rather than contract-driven, and status can drift from validity dates.
- Affected models: Subscription, CheckoutDraft, Delivery, delivery-related config models introduced later, Payment
- Affected APIs: quote, checkout, delivery update, menu/catalog delivery payloads, admin delivery management APIs
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, menuController, adminController, kitchenController, notification/scheduler services
- Migration considerations: existing delivery subscriptions remain grandfathered unless an explicit migration policy is later approved; old subscriptions keep flat-fee contract markers
- Backward compatibility concerns: delivery reads must support both legacy flat-fee contracts and new zone contracts during the coexistence period
- Operational/dashboard impact: admin can reason about delivery commitments correctly; expired subscriptions stay historically visible but operationally inactive
- Risks: address-to-zone logic, grandfather boundaries, and dashboard filtering changes can create operational confusion if not explicit
- Dependencies: Phase 1

**Phase 6 — Freeze, Skip, Compensation, Refund Windows, and Cancellation Semantics**
- Classification: must-do for correctness, but later than the core phases
- Objective: align freeze and skip as separate actions, add compensated skip behavior, and define refundable-returnable windows for one-time day add-ons.
- Why this phase is needed: current freeze exists, skip exists, but compensated skip is not implemented and current skip behavior directly deducts meals with no compensation extension.
- Affected models: Subscription, SubscriptionDay, Payment, contract policy snapshot fields
- Affected APIs: freeze, unfreeze, skip, unskip, skip-range, admin cancel/extend, one-time add-on cancel/refund handling
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, subscriptionService, adminController, fulfillmentService
- Migration considerations: grandfathered subscriptions may keep old skip behavior until explicit conversion; compensated skip should be opt-in by contract version
- Backward compatibility concerns: active users may already rely on current uncompensated skip behavior
- Operational/dashboard impact: support and admin will finally have contract-consistent answers for skipped, frozen, and pre-preparation canceled days
- Risks: this phase changes entitlement timing and calendar validity behavior; it is highly support-sensitive
- Dependencies: Phases 1 through 5

**Phase 7 — Ledger, Projection, and Deletion-Safety Hardening**
- Classification: recommended for maintainability
- Objective: move high-churn wallet/planning activity toward clearer ledgers and projections, and prevent hard-delete damage to historical readability.
- Why this phase is needed: current historical readability is fragile because plans/meals can be deleted while locked and fulfilled records mostly keep IDs, not fully denormalized views.
- Affected models: Subscription, SubscriptionDay, Payment, activity/read-model or ledger additions later
- Affected APIs: wallet history, admin reporting, kitchen/admin subscription detail reads
- Affected services/controllers: subscriptionController, adminController, kitchenController, reporting services
- Migration considerations: dual-read or projection backfill will be needed; historical records should be enriched without rewriting business meaning
- Backward compatibility concerns: old records must remain readable during projection backfill
- Operational/dashboard impact: support, finance, and operations get safer historical reporting
- Risks: dual-write drift if introduced too early
- Dependencies: core phases complete and stable

**Phase 8 — Capacity, Dispatch, and Multi-Branch Growth**
- Classification: optional future enhancement
- Objective: add slot capacity, dispatch workflows, and future branch expansion after the core model is stable.
- Why this phase is needed: these features are valuable, but they should not block correctness work.
- Affected models: delivery/dispatch capacity and branch models introduced later
- Affected APIs: slot availability, courier assignment, future multi-branch pickup APIs
- Affected services/controllers: delivery/admin/courier services
- Migration considerations: feature-flagged rollout only
- Backward compatibility concerns: should not alter existing contract behavior unless explicitly enabled
- Operational/dashboard impact: stronger logistics planning and scalability
- Risks: implementing this too early would multiply complexity before the contract model stabilizes
- Dependencies: Phases 1 through 7

**2. What changed compared to the old phased plan**
- Previous assumption no longer correct: premium overage was an open policy question. New source of truth: premium overage must be an immediate paid flow during planning and the day cannot be confirmed until it is paid.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: add-on taxonomy and behavior were still partly open. New source of truth: recurring add-ons are daily entitlements, currently limited to one item per category per day, and one-time add-ons are paid day-level purchases only.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: no-planning fallback behavior was partly undecided. New source of truth: auto-assignment may use regular meals only, must include recurring daily add-ons, must not consume premium automatically, and must not auto-add one-time add-ons.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: renewal was treated as an optional later capability. New source of truth: same-plan renewal is now part of the foundation and belongs in Phase 1 design.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: compensated skip was an open design area. New source of truth: compensated skip is approved, but it is explicitly later than the core phases.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: existing delivery subscriptions had an unclear migration path. New source of truth: existing delivery subscriptions should remain grandfathered unless a separate migration policy is explicitly approved.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: recurring add-ons might roll or behave like wallet balances. New source of truth: recurring add-ons are daily entitlements and do not roll forward.
- Previous assumption no longer correct: start date fallback was not fixed. New source of truth: default start date is tomorrow.

**3. Phase 1 technical design**

**1. Scope**
- Canonical contract snapshot for all newly created subscriptions and pending subscription activations.
- Tomorrow-default start date when no explicit startDate is supplied.
- Contract alignment between customer checkout and admin-created subscriptions.
- Unification of webhook verify, manual verify, and activation side effects.
- Idempotency consistency across all paid write flows that already exist today.
- Explicit grandfathering boundaries for legacy subscriptions.
- Renewal-on-same-plan support if the prior plan configuration is still currently sellable.
- Phase 1 does not implement the new premium wallet, add-on entitlement model, zone delivery runtime, or compensated skip behavior.

**2. Target behavior**
- Every new subscription contract is built once, versioned, and stored before activation.
- Every activated subscription stores the exact purchased contract snapshot, not just scattered runtime fields.
- Omitting startDate resolves to tomorrow in KSA time.
- Customer checkout and admin-created subscriptions both use the same contract builder and the same subscription activation pathway.
- Webhook verification and manual verification both end in the same payment-application function and the same activation function.
- Existing subscriptions remain grandfathered; they stay readable and operational under legacy rules unless explicitly migrated later.
- Renewal uses the previous subscription’s contract snapshot when available, and falls back to legacy fields only when safe.

**3. Exact current-code problems this phase solves**
- No full immutable subscription contract snapshot exists today.
- checkoutSubscription, createSubscriptionAdmin, finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment, verifyCheckoutDraftPayment, webhook activation, and admin payment verification all create or apply subscription state through different paths.
- Default start date currently falls back to new Date() rather than tomorrow.
- Idempotency is strong for subscription checkout, but inconsistent or absent for top-ups and one-time add-on payment initiation.
- Freeze policy and some contract behavior still depend on mutable Plan or settings data.
- Existing subscriptions are not explicitly marked as legacy/grandfathered contract types.
- Renewal is not modeled as a first-class contract-driven flow.

**4. Target contract snapshot structure**
- meta: contract version, creation timestamp, creation source, actor type, grandfathering mode, compatibility mode
- origin: customer_checkout, admin_create, or renewal; optional previous subscription reference; optional admin override reason
- plan: plan reference ID, plan display name at purchase time, daysCount, selectedGrams, mealsPerDay, total base meals, currency
- start: requested start date, resolved start date, default rule applied flag, timezone basis
- pricing: base plan price, delivery fee, VAT percentage, VAT amount, total amount, currency, quoted-at timestamp
- deliveryContract: delivery mode, pricing mode, grandfathered mode flag, slot type/window/slot ID, pickup branch identity if pickup, zone identity if zone-delivery is later introduced, address snapshot
- policySnapshot: freeze policy, current skip policy mode, cutoff policy mode, fallback mode, premium auto-consumption rule, one-time add-on confirmation rule
- entitlementContract: placeholder future-proof section for premium, recurring add-ons, and other purchasable entitlements; in Phase 1 this can be populated in compatibility form while runtime still uses legacy fields
- compatibilityRefs: original plan ID, current runtime compatibility markers, legacy source markers if derived rather than first-class

**5. Which existing models need additions only**
- CheckoutDraft: add contract snapshot, contract version, contract hash, creation source, renewal reference, grandfathering marker, admin override metadata
- Subscription: add contract snapshot, contract version, contract hash, creation source, renewal reference, grandfathered legacy flag, snapshot completeness marker
- Payment: add operation idempotency fields for non-checkout paid writes, normalized request hash, operation kind, and operation reference metadata
- No destructive schema replacement is part of Phase 1; all additions are additive and legacy fields remain intact

**6. Which existing flows must read from snapshot instead of mutable plan/settings**
- Subscription activation must read daysCount, selected plan dimensions, resolved start date, delivery contract, and quoted pricing from the snapshot rather than live plan/settings
- Freeze and unfreeze policy lookup for new subscriptions must read from contractSnapshot.policySnapshot.freezePolicy, not the current Plan.freezePolicy
- User/admin serialization for new subscriptions should read displayable plan/delivery contract details from snapshot
- Renewal prefill must read from the previous subscription snapshot when available
- Any future determination of grandfathered delivery mode must read from snapshot, not infer from current settings
- Phase 1 does not yet move premium/add-on runtime logic to snapshot; it only establishes the contract source of truth that later phases will consume

**7. Idempotency model for all paid write flows**
- Every paid initiation request must carry an idempotency key
- Every paid initiation request must generate a canonical request hash from actor, operation type, and business payload
- Subscription checkout keeps the draft-based idempotency pattern but now stores the canonical contract hash
- Existing top-up and one-time add-on payment initiations gain the same idempotency contract using Payment metadata and additive idempotency fields
- Replays with the same idempotency key and same hash return the existing pending/finalized result
- Replays with the same idempotency key and different hash return a conflict
- Provider retries remain harmless because side effects are still guarded by a single payment.applied claim step
- Future premium-overage and one-time-planning-payment flows will inherit the same idempotency model, but they are not implemented in Phase 1

**8. How customer checkout, admin create, webhook verify, and manual verify should converge**
- One shared contract builder resolves request input into a canonical snapshot
- One shared activation function creates the subscription and initial days from the stored snapshot
- Customer checkout uses the contract builder, persists a draft plus payment initiation, then waits for payment settlement
- Admin-created subscriptions use the same contract builder and the same activation function, but with explicit admin source metadata and optional admin-only override annotations
- Manual verification and webhook verification both do only two things: synchronize provider payment state, then call one shared “claim and apply side effects” function
- The shared payment side-effect function decides whether to activate a subscription, apply a top-up, or apply a paid day add-on based on normalized stored metadata only
- This removes the current duplication between controller verify paths and webhook logic

**9. Renewal flow design using previous subscription data**
- Renewal is based on previous subscription identity, not just free-form plan selection
- If the previous subscription has a contract snapshot, the renewal seed comes from that snapshot
- If the previous subscription has no snapshot, the renewal seed can be derived only from safe legacy fields: planId, selectedGrams, selectedMealsPerDay, and current delivery preference
- Renewal must validate that the referenced plan is still active and that the same grams/meals-per-day option is still sellable
- If the old plan shape is not still available, renewal fails cleanly and the user must choose a new plan manually
- Phase 1 renewal should copy the base plan contract only; it should not silently repurchase premium balances, one-time add-ons, or later-phase recurring entitlement models
- Renewal uses the same contract builder and checkout/admin creation path as a normal new subscription

**10. Backward compatibility strategy**
- Existing subscriptions without snapshots are explicitly treated as legacy contracts
- Legacy subscriptions continue to read existing runtime fields until later phases move them
- New subscriptions created after Phase 1 always write a snapshot
- Legacy delivery subscriptions remain flat-fee grandfathered and are not zone-migrated in Phase 1
- Legacy premium and add-on runtime behavior is not migrated in Phase 1, even if new snapshots begin carrying future-proof contract sections
- APIs should continue returning legacy-derived fields while the new snapshot fields are added progressively

**11. Migration/backfill strategy**
- Add snapshot fields without forcing immediate backfill
- Backfill recent drafts and active subscriptions only when the source data is reliable enough
- Mark backfilled snapshots with completeness states such as full, derived, or partial-legacy
- If a referenced plan has been deleted or mutated too far, store a partial snapshot marker and keep legacy runtime reads active for that subscription
- Do not mutate wallet balances, add-on state, or delivery runtime behavior in Phase 1
- Do not attempt to reinterpret legacy premium/add-on semantics during Phase 1 backfill

**12. Rollout strategy**
- First write canonical snapshots for new drafts and new admin-created subscriptions while leaving legacy reads untouched
- Then switch new subscription activation to consume the snapshot only
- Then unify manual verify and webhook apply paths behind one side-effect function
- Then enable same-plan renewal using the new snapshot-first read path
- Keep observability around snapshot build vs. legacy resolved values during the coexistence period
- Expose grandfathered/legacy contract markers in admin tooling early so support can distinguish old and new behaviors

**13. Risks and rollback considerations**
- The largest risk is activating from a snapshot that does not match the legacy fields currently expected by downstream logic
- Another high risk is duplicate application during the cutover from duplicated verification logic to one shared application path
- Renewal can fail unexpectedly if historical plans were hard-deleted or current grams/meals options were removed
- Partial snapshot backfills can create false confidence if not visibly marked as derived/legacy
- Rollback must be able to ignore new snapshot fields and continue using legacy runtime fields without data loss
- Phase 1 must therefore be additive, reversible, and observable

**14. What must explicitly NOT be changed yet in Phase 1**
- Do not change premium runtime behavior to generic wallet consumption yet
- Do not implement premium overage payment yet
- Do not convert add-ons to daily category entitlements yet
- Do not implement one-time add-on confirmation gating yet
- Do not move delivery to zone pricing yet
- Do not implement compensated skip yet
- Do not rewrite automation fallback yet beyond carrying forward contract-read foundations
- Do not replace current historical snapshot contents yet
- Do not remove legacy bridges yet

**4. Phase 1 risks**
- Snapshot drift risk: new snapshots may disagree with today’s scattered runtime fields if the contract builder is not the only source of purchase truth.
- Activation race risk: webhook, user verify, and admin verify currently overlap; unification must preserve strict single-apply behavior.
- Grandfathering ambiguity risk: if legacy subscriptions are not explicitly labeled, later phases will accidentally mix contract models.
- Renewal safety risk: deleted plans and removed grams/meals options can make “same-plan renewal” impossible unless failure behavior is explicit.
- Admin divergence risk: if admin-created subscriptions keep bypassing the canonical builder, Phase 1 loses most of its value immediately.
- Partial backfill risk: derived snapshots for older subscriptions can be mistaken for authoritative purchase contracts if completeness is not exposed clearly.

**5. Phase 1 approval checklist**
- Approve that all new subscriptions must store a versioned canonical contract snapshot before activation.
- Approve that omitted startDate resolves to tomorrow in KSA time.
- Approve that customer checkout and admin-created subscriptions must use the same contract builder and activation path.
- Approve that webhook verify and manual verify must converge on one shared payment side-effect application path.
- Approve additive idempotency for all existing paid initiation flows, not just subscription checkout.
- Approve that existing subscriptions are explicitly labeled legacy/grandfathered rather than silently inferred later.
- Approve that same-plan renewal in Phase 1 is limited to reusing the prior base plan configuration when it is still sellable.
- Approve that renewal in Phase 1 does not automatically repurchase premium balances or one-time add-ons.
- Approve that legacy premium, add-on, delivery, and skip behavior remain unchanged in Phase 1.
- Approve that partial snapshot backfills are allowed but must be visibly marked and must not override legacy behavior.

**1. Task-by-task implementation breakdown**

**Task 1: Define Phase 1 contract snapshot contract**
- Goal: finalize the exact snapshot shape and metadata conventions before touching flow logic.
- Output: one internal contract schema definition for CheckoutDraft and Subscription, including versioning, source, grandfathering marker, completeness marker, contract hash, and renewal metadata.
- Notes: this task must encode your clarification that previous delivery preferences are only a renewal seed, not a forced future delivery contract.

هذا الرد

**Task 2: Build one canonical contract builder**
- Goal: create a single contract-construction path that resolves request input into a normalized Phase 1 snapshot.
- Output: one builder that both customer checkout and admin-created subscriptions call.
- Scope in Phase 1: plan selection, grams, meals-per-day, start date defaulting to tomorrow, flat/grandfathered delivery contract shape, pricing breakdown snapshot, policy snapshot, origin metadata.
- Out of scope in Phase 1: premium redesign, add-on redesign, zone delivery runtime.

**Task 3: Introduce explicit contract versioning and grandfather labeling**
- Goal: ensure all new subscriptions are clearly “Phase 1 canonical contract” and all old subscriptions are explicitly legacy/grandfathered.
- Output: contract version markers and legacy labeling rules on write and read.
- Notes: old subscriptions should not be auto-converted in behavior.

**Task 4: Change checkout draft creation to store the contract snapshot**
- Goal: make CheckoutDraft the first persisted canonical contract artifact.
- Output: customer checkout creates drafts from the canonical builder and stores snapshot + hash + metadata.
- Notes: quote still remains separate, but checkout must persist the exact contract that will later activate.

**Task 5: Align admin-created subscriptions to the same contract builder**
- Goal: remove contract drift between customer-created and admin-created subscriptions.
- Output: admin create subscription uses the same builder and the same activation pathway, with admin-only metadata/override markers.
- Notes: admin-only overrides must be explicit in the stored contract metadata, not hidden in controller logic.

**Task 6: Create one activation/apply path for subscription creation**
- Goal: converge subscription activation regardless of whether it comes from webhook, manual verify, or admin create.
- Output: one shared activation function that consumes the stored snapshot and creates the subscription + day rows.
- Notes: this is the core Phase 1 refactor boundary.

**Task 7: Unify payment side-effect application**
- Goal: webhook verification, manual verification, and admin verification all end in one shared “claim and apply” flow.
- Output: one payment side-effect dispatcher that routes to subscription activation or existing top-up/day-payment handlers.
- Notes: keep current premium/add-on/day-payment business behavior unchanged, only unify the path.

**Task 8: Extend idempotency to all paid initiation flows**
- Goal: make top-ups and one-time paid add-ons follow the same idempotency discipline as checkout.
- Output: standard idempotency key parsing, request hashing, and replay/conflict behavior across paid initiation endpoints.
- Notes: this is additive and must not change provider-side payment semantics.

**Task 9: Implement tomorrow-default start-date behavior**
- Goal: when startDate is omitted, resolve to tomorrow in KSA consistently for customer checkout and admin create.
- Output: one resolver used by the contract builder.
- Notes: this is a real business behavior change in Phase 1 and should be tested heavily.

**Task 10: Add same-plan renewal seed flow**
- Goal: support renewal by reusing the previous base-plan configuration when still sellable.
- Output: a renewal seed flow that derives plan/grams/meals-per-day from prior snapshot if present, otherwise safe legacy fields.
- Notes: previous delivery preference may be used only as a prefill seed when safe; it must not silently force future delivery behavior.

**Task 11: Add snapshot-aware read serialization for new contracts**
- Goal: expose enough contract metadata in admin/user reads to make support and debugging possible.
- Output: serialization reads snapshot first for new subscriptions, while legacy subscriptions still read legacy fields.
- Notes: do not replace legacy response fields yet unless additive.

**Task 12: Add partial backfill support and completeness markers**
- Goal: allow safe optional backfill for existing rows without changing runtime behavior.
- Output: backfill policy and markers such as full, derived, legacy_unavailable.
- Notes: this should be read-only safe and never flip behavior for old subscriptions.
