**3. Recommended refactor boundaries for Phase 1 only**

These are the safe boundaries for this phase. Anything outside them should wait.

**Boundary A: Contract construction**
- Move only contract-building logic into a dedicated service.
- Keep current business pricing rules intact.
- Do not redesign premium/add-on semantics inside this service yet.

**Boundary B: Subscription activation**
- Centralize creation of Subscription and SubscriptionDay rows from a stored contract snapshot.
- This should replace duplicated activation code paths.
- Do not change planning, freeze, skip, or fulfillment behavior here yet.

**Boundary C: Payment side-effect application**
- Centralize “claim payment and apply business side effects”.
- Keep existing side-effect types the same in Phase 1:
  - subscription activation
  - premium top-up
  - add-on top-up
  - one-time add-on
  - custom day purchases
- Do not redesign the meaning of those payment types yet.

**Boundary D: Idempotency**
- Standardize only initiation-time idempotency.
- Do not redesign provider reconciliation logic beyond routing everything through one apply path.

**Boundary E: Renewal seed resolution**
- Add a focused renewal service that only resolves reusable base-plan inputs.
- Do not let renewal mutate contract semantics for delivery, premium, or add-ons.

What should not be refactored in Phase 1:
- Day planning architecture
- Premium wallet semantics
- Add-on entitlement model
- Delivery zone modeling
- Freeze/skip compensation rules
- Kitchen/automation business behavior beyond contract-read foundations

---

**4. Sequencing of changes inside Phase 1**

**Step 1: Lock the data contract**
- Finalize snapshot fields, versioning rules, grandfather markers, completeness markers, and renewal metadata.
- Decide exact naming once, because later phases will build on it.

**Step 2: Build the canonical contract builder**
- Resolve input into snapshot shape.
- Apply tomorrow default for omitted startDate.
- Preserve current pricing and delivery logic as-is for new contracts in Phase 1.

**Step 3: Make checkout draft persist the canonical snapshot**
- Customer checkout stores the contract snapshot and contract hash.
- Existing response shape remains stable where possible.

**Step 4: Build the activation service**
- New subscription creation and day creation move behind one shared activation path that consumes snapshot only.

**Step 5: Move admin-created subscriptions onto the same activation path**
- Admin create becomes a canonical writer too.
- Admin-only metadata is captured explicitly.

**Step 6: Unify manual verify and webhook apply**
- Both verification paths call the same payment application service.
- Preserve payment.applied claiming semantics.

**Step 7: Extend idempotency to all paid initiation flows**
- Apply the shared idempotency model to top-ups and one-time day-paid flows.
- Keep existing business meaning unchanged.

**Step 8: Add renewal seed flow**
- Support lookup of a previous subscription and produce a new canonical contract seed.
- Validate that the same plan option is still available.

**Step 9: Add snapshot-aware reads**
- Serialization prefers snapshot for new subscriptions and keeps legacy behavior for old ones.
- Add admin-visible legacy/grandfather markers.

**Step 10: Optional backfill tooling and guarded rollout**
- Add partial backfill only after the new write path is stable.
- Never let backfill change runtime behavior.

---

**5. Test strategy for Phase 1**

**A. Contract builder tests**
- Omitted startDate resolves to tomorrow in KSA time.
- Explicit valid startDate is preserved.
- Invalid startDate is rejected consistently.
- Contract hash is stable for semantically identical payloads.
- Renewal seed from prior snapshot reproduces the same base-plan selection.
- Renewal fails cleanly if prior plan option is no longer available.
- Previous delivery preference is treated only as optional seed data, not forced contract behavior.

**B. Checkout and draft tests**
- Checkout stores a contract snapshot on the draft.
- Repeating the same checkout with the same idempotency key reuses the same draft/payment result.
- Same idempotency key with different payload returns conflict.
- Same request hash with pending checkout behaves as expected.

**C. Activation tests**
- Activation from draft snapshot creates subscription fields correctly.
- Initial subscription days are generated from snapshot dimensions.
- Snapshot data, not mutable live plan fields, drives activation for new subscriptions.
- Admin create and customer checkout produce equivalent snapshot-backed subscriptions for the same payload.

**D. Verification convergence tests**
- Webhook “paid” and manual verify both converge to one activation result.
- Duplicate webhook/manual verify attempts do not double-create subscriptions.
- Non-paid terminal statuses update draft/payment state consistently.
- Existing top-up and one-time payment types still apply exactly once.

**E. Legacy/grandfather tests**
- Existing subscriptions without snapshots continue to read and behave as before.
- New subscriptions are labeled as canonical Phase 1 contracts.
- Partial backfill markers do not alter runtime behavior.

**F. Renewal tests**
- Renewal from prior canonical subscription succeeds when the same plan option is still active.
- Renewal from prior legacy subscription uses safe legacy fields only.
- Renewal does not silently carry premium balances, add-ons, or future delivery semantics.

**G. Regression tests around unchanged behavior**
- Premium runtime behavior remains itemized/legacy as before.
- Add-on runtime behavior remains unchanged.
- Freeze/skip behavior remains unchanged.
- Delivery flat-fee behavior for existing subscriptions remains unchanged.

Recommended test layers:
- unit tests for builder/hash/seed logic
- service-level tests for activation and payment application
- controller/integration tests for checkout, admin create, webhook verify, manual verify, and renewal initiation
- migration tests for partial backfill safety

---

**6. Rollout and verification checklist**

**Pre-rollout**
- Confirm final Phase 1 contract schema and version string.
- Confirm legacy/grandfather marker semantics.
- Confirm renewal fallback behavior for deleted or unavailable plans.
- Confirm idempotency behavior for all paid initiation endpoints.
- Confirm tomorrow-default date behavior with exact KSA timezone handling.

**Deployment verification**
- New customer checkout writes a draft snapshot.
- New admin-created subscription writes the same contract shape.
- A paid checkout activates through the shared apply path exactly once.
- Manual verify and webhook verify yield the same final subscription state.
- Top-up and one-time paid initiation endpoints accept and enforce idempotency.
- New subscriptions expose canonical contract markers in admin reads.
- Existing legacy subscriptions still serialize and operate unchanged.

**Post-rollout monitoring**
- Count of new subscriptions with missing snapshot should be zero.
- Count of duplicate applied payments should remain zero.
- Count of idempotency conflicts should be monitored, not ignored.
- Renewal failure reasons should be logged distinctly:
  - plan missing
  - grams option missing
  - meals-per-day option missing
  - legacy source insufficient
- Snapshot-vs-legacy divergence logs should be reviewed for a short stabilization window.

**Operational validation**
- Support can tell whether a subscription is legacy or canonical.
- Admin can see the stored start date and whether it was defaulted.
- Admin can tell whether a subscription originated from checkout, admin create, or renewal.

---

**7. Explicit “safe to do now” vs “must wait until later phases”**

**Safe to do now**
- Add contract snapshot fields and version markers.
- Add grandfather/legacy markers.
- Add snapshot completeness markers for backfills.
- Build a shared contract builder.
- Build a shared activation path.
- Unify webhook/manual/admin payment application paths.
- Add idempotency to all paid initiation endpoints.
- Change omitted startDate default to tomorrow in KSA.
- Add renewal seed flow for same-plan renewal only.
- Prefer snapshot reads for new subscriptions while leaving legacy reads intact.
- Add admin/support visibility for canonical vs legacy contracts.

**Must wait until later phases**
- Generic premium wallet implementation.
- Paid premium overage flow during planning.
- Category-based recurring add-on entitlement model.
- One-time add-on confirmation gating during planning.
- Exact day-planning redesign and slot model.
- Zone-based delivery runtime and admin zone management.
- Compensated skip implementation.
- Refund-return logic for one-time add-ons on cancel/freeze/skip.
- Historical denormalization redesign for locked/fulfilled records.
- Removal of legacy premium/add-on bridges.
- Any behavior change to current active legacy subscriptions beyond explicit Phase 1 contract labeling and safe read/write additions.

If you want, the next step can be a very concrete engineering workboard for Phase 1 in the form of:
task id | goal | files | owner boundary | test cases | rollout dependency
without moving into code yet.

For each task include:
- task id
- task name
- objective
- exact files likely touched
- new files/modules to create if any
- dependency on previous tasks
- risk level (low / medium / high)
- test cases required
- rollout notes
- clear definition of done

Also separate tasks into:
1. safe foundational tasks first
2. shared-path convergence tasks
3. rollout/compatibility tasks
4. optional backfill tasks

Important constraints:
- keep Phase 1 strictly limited to canonical contract, payment consistency, idempotency, tomorrow-default start date, grandfather labeling, admin/customer alignment, shared activation/apply path, and same-plan renewal seed flow
- do not include premium redesign
- do not include add-on redesign
- do not include zone delivery implementation
- do not include planning redesign
- do not include freeze/skip redesign
- do not include controller-wide cosmetic refactors

At the end include:
1. recommended implementation order
2. minimum safe merge slices
3. what can be feature-flagged
4. what should be shipped together in one release
5. pre-code approval checklist

Do not implement code yet.
Do not move to Phase 2.

- objective: Provide a safe, clearly marked backfill path for legacy subscriptions where contract data can be derived without changing runtime behavior.
- exact files likely touched: [Subscription.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Subscription.js), [CheckoutDraft.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/CheckoutDraft.js)
- new files/modules to create if any: [subscriptionSnapshotBackfillService.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/subscriptionSnapshotBackfillService.js), [backfillSubscriptionSnapshots.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/scripts/backfillSubscriptionSnapshots.js)
- dependency on previous tasks: P1-W01, P1-W11
- risk level: medium
- test cases required: dry-run report accuracy; partial snapshots are marked correctly; backfilled legacy subscriptions do not switch behavior; deleted-plan cases are reported as incomplete rather than guessed
- rollout notes: do not block Phase 1 release on this task; run only after new-write paths are stable
- clear definition of done: a dry-run and guarded write mode exist for partial backfill, and all backfilled rows are clearly marked as non-authoritative legacy-derived data

**5. Recommended implementation order**
1. P1-W01
2. P1-W02
3. P1-W03
4. P1-W04
5. P1-W05
6. P1-W06
7. P1-W07
8. P1-W08
9. P1-W11
10. P1-W12
11. P1-W09
12. P1-W10
13. P1-W13

Reason for this order:
- Model and utility groundwork first
- Shared activation/apply path before broader rollout
- Read/visibility and flags before wider adoption
- Non-checkout idempotency and renewal after the core contract path is stable
- Backfill last

**6. Minimum safe merge slices**
1. Slice A: P1-W01 + P1-W02 + P1-W03
   - additive schema and internal utilities only
2. Slice B: P1-W04 + P1-W05
   - shared activation service plus checkout draft snapshot write behind flags
3. Slice C: P1-W06 + P1-W07 + P1-W08
   - admin alignment plus shared payment-apply convergence
4. Slice D: P1-W11 + P1-W12
   - snapshot-aware reads, grandfather exposure, observability, feature flags
5. Slice E: P1-W09
   - non-checkout paid-flow idempotency
6. Slice F: P1-W10
   - renewal seed flow behind its own flag
7. Slice G: P1-W13
   - optional backfill tooling only

**7. What can be feature-flagged**
- Canonical snapshot write on checkout drafts
- Shared snapshot activation path
- Unified payment application path
- Snapshot-first reads for canonical subscriptions
- Strict idempotency enforcement for top-ups and one-time paid add-ons
- Same-plan renewal seed flow
- Backfill write mode

**8. What should be shipped together in one release**
- P1-W04 + P1-W05 + P1-W06 + P1-W07 + P1-W08 + P1-W11 + P1-W12
- These belong together because they define the new canonical contract write path, activation path, payment application path, and the minimum read/visibility safeguards needed to operate them safely.
- P1-W09 can ship in the same release if the team is comfortable expanding idempotency surface area immediately.
- P1-W10 can be held behind a flag and enabled after the core release stabilizes.
- P1-W13 should not be required for the first Phase 1 release.

- Approve that optional backfills are explicitly non-authoritative and must not alter legacy runtime behavior.

**4. Migration safety notes**

- All new schema fields in Slice A should be additive and nullable/optional.
- No legacy subscription or draft should be required to have contractSnapshot, contractVersion, or contractHash.
- Slice A should not perform any backfill automatically.
- Slice A should not switch any runtime business behavior for legacy subscriptions.
- contractSnapshot should be stored as Mixed in Phase 1 for safety and to avoid brittle migration coupling while the foundation is still being introduced.
- New Payment idempotency fields should not change existing payment application behavior yet.
- If unique indexes are added for Payment.operationIdempotencyKey, do so only after the idempotency scope decision is confirmed.
- Existing checkout draft idempotency fields (idempotencyKey, requestHash) should remain intact in Slice A; contractHash is additive, not a replacement yet.
- No Slice A logic should branch operationally on contractMode yet, except safe metadata exposure later.

**5. Test list for Slice A**

**Model-level tests**
- CheckoutDraft can persist all new Phase 1 contract fields
- Subscription can persist all new Phase 1 contract fields
- Payment can persist all new idempotency fields
- legacy documents without any of the new fields still read successfully

**Contract builder tests**
- omitted startDate resolves to tomorrow in KSA
- explicit future startDate is preserved
- invalid or past startDate still fails correctly
- contract snapshot includes approved fixed fields and metadata
- plan.totalMeals equals daysCount * mealsPerDay
- contractHash is stable for the same effective canonical contract
- localized plan name capture is correct

**Idempotency service tests**
- same key + same effective payload => "reuse"
- same key + different effective payload => "conflict"
- same effective payload with normalized key formatting produces the same request hash
- different operation scopes produce different request hashes even with the same business payload
- buildContractHash ignores irrelevant transport noise and stays stable on canonical input

**Regression safety tests**
- existing checkout draft fields still work unchanged
- no webhook/manual verify behavior changes occur in Slice A
- no admin create behavior changes occur in Slice A unless explicitly wired

**Timezone boundary tests**
- requests near KSA midnight still default to the correct “tomorrow”
- bare date inputs and ISO date inputs normalize consistently to KSA date logic

---

**6. Anything ambiguous that still needs explicit approval before coding**

Two items are still important enough to confirm before coding Slice A:

**A. Payment idempotency scope**
Recommended option:
- uniqueness and replay/conflict should be scoped by:
  - userId + operationScope + operationIdempotencyKey
Why I recommend it:
- it prevents accidental conflicts where a user reuses the same key for unrelated paid actions like checkout and premium top-up
Alternative:
- userId + operationIdempotencyKey globally across all paid operations
This is stricter, but more likely to create surprising conflicts.

**B. contractHash basis**
Recommended option:
- contractHash should be derived from the canonical business contract only
- request idempotency hash should be derived from:
  - userId + operationScope + effectivePayload
Why I recommend it:
- it keeps contract identity reusable across customer checkout, admin create, and future renewal flows
- while still keeping idempotent request handling actor- and operation-scoped

If you approve those two points, Slice A is fully specified and ready for coding without moving beyond it.

5. **Risk review**
Hidden risks introduced by Slice A:
- subscriptionContractService currently allows payload.vatPercentage to influence snapshot pricing if supplied. Since this is not wired yet, it is not active risk now, but it could create divergence later if reused carelessly.
- contractSnapshot is Mixed, which is intentionally flexible, but that also means shape mistakes will not be schema-enforced.
- The enum-backed contract metadata fields are safe now, but future writes will fail validation if callers send unsupported values.
- operationScope on Payment is intentionally not enum-restricted, which is flexible but less strict for future callers.
- The exported helper normalizeForHashing is broader than strictly necessary; harmless now, but it expands the public surface area.

package.json / test-runner impact:
- Added "test": "node --test" in [package.json](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/package.json)
- Low risk if CI already runs npm test
- Medium risk only if the current CI or deployment tooling assumes there is no test script, or if some environments use older Node versions without stable node:test
- In this repo, the test runner change is otherwise isolated and non-runtime

6. **Ready-for-merge assessment**
- safe to merge with minor follow-up

Why briefly:
- The Slice A code is additive, dark, legacy-safe, and not wired into live behavior.
- The main follow-up I’d want before relying on it heavily is a small extra test pass for KSA-midnight boundary cases and a quick decision later on whether payload.vatPercentage should remain in the contract builder once Slice B wiring begins.

ده الرد 
1. **Scope of Slice B**
- Implement P1-W04 and P1-W05 only.
- Add canonical contract snapshot writing to new customer checkout drafts.
- Add a shared activation service that can create a subscription from a canonical draft snapshot.
- Use that activation service only from the existing customer-checkout subscription-finalization path.
- Keep webhook/manual verification entrypoints as they are.
- Keep admin-created subscription runtime as it is.
- Do not redesign premium, add-ons, delivery, planning, or skip/freeze behavior.

2. **Exact behavior changes introduced by Slice B**
- New customer checkout drafts will store:
  - contractVersion
  - contractMode
  - contractCompleteness
  - contractSource
  - contractHash
  - contractSnapshot
  - renewedFromSubscriptionId when applicable later
- New customer checkout drafts will be built from the Phase 1 canonical contract builder.
- New customer checkouts with omitted startDate will now resolve to tomorrow in KSA for canonical drafts.
- New subscriptions activated from canonical checkout drafts will copy the canonical contract fields onto the created Subscription.
- New canonical subscriptions will be activated from the stored snapshot instead of reconstructing from scattered draft fields.
- Existing API response shapes should remain unchanged for checkout/initiation.
- Legacy drafts and legacy subscriptions remain on the old activation logic.

3. **Exact files likely to change**
- [subscriptionController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js)
- [subscriptionContractService.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/subscriptionContractService.js)
- [CheckoutDraft.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/CheckoutDraft.js)
- [Subscription.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/models/Subscription.js)

Test files likely to be added or updated:
- [subscriptionContractService.test.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/test/subscriptionContractService.test.js)
- new activation service test file, likely [subscriptionActivationService.test.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/test/subscriptionActivationService.test.js)
- new checkout/finalization slice tests, likely [checkoutSliceB.test.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/test/checkoutSliceB.test.js) or similar

Files that should probably not change in Slice B:
- [adminController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js)
- [webhookController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js)
- routes unless a test helper or export requires it

4. **New modules/services to create or extend**
- Create src/services/subscriptionActivationService.js
  - purpose: activate a subscription from a canonical checkout draft snapshot
  - recommended primary function:
    - activateSubscriptionFromCanonicalDraft({ draft, payment, session })
- Extend src/services/subscriptionContractService.js
  - only if needed for a small helper that maps a built canonical contract into draft-write fields
  - avoid broad expansion
- Optional small flag helper if not already present:
  - src/utils/featureFlags.js
  - only if needed to keep Slice B narrow and reversible

5. **Feature-flag strategy for Slice B**
- Recommended flags:
  - PHASE1_CANONICAL_CHECKOUT_DRAFT_WRITE
  - PHASE1_CANONICAL_DRAFT_ACTIVATION
- Behavior:
  - if PHASE1_CANONICAL_CHECKOUT_DRAFT_WRITE is off:
    - checkout draft behavior remains fully legacy
  - if PHASE1_CANONICAL_CHECKOUT_DRAFT_WRITE is on:
    - checkout draft stores canonical contract fields
  - if PHASE1_CANONICAL_DRAFT_ACTIVATION is off:
    - finalization still uses legacy activation logic
  - if PHASE1_CANONICAL_DRAFT_ACTIVATION is on:
    - only canonical drafts with valid snapshot/version use snapshot activation
    - legacy drafts continue using the existing activation path
- This lets us canary draft writing before enabling snapshot-based activation.

6. **How checkout draft writing will change**
- checkoutSubscription will keep its current flow:
  - parse idempotency key
  - resolve quote
  - compute existing legacy requestHash
  - perform existing idempotency lookups
- After quote resolution, if the write flag is enabled:
  - call buildPhase1SubscriptionContract(...) with:
    - payload: req.body
    - resolvedQuote: quote
    - actorContext: { actorRole: "client", actorUserId: req.userId }
    - source: "customer_checkout"
    - now: new Date()
  - persist the returned canonical contract fields on CheckoutDraft
- Existing legacy draft fields should still be written too:
  - planId
  - daysCount
  - grams
  - mealsPerDay
  - delivery
  - premiumItems
  - addonItems
  - addonSubscriptions
  - breakdown
- Existing idempotencyKey and requestHash remain unchanged in Slice B.
- Recommended behavior for draft.startDate:
  - use the canonical resolved start date for canonical drafts so draft top-level data and snapshot do not diverge

7. **How shared activation from snapshot will work**
- Add a new activation service that takes an already-paid canonical draft and creates:
  - Subscription
  - initial SubscriptionDay rows
- Activation inputs come from:
  - draft.contractSnapshot
  - draft.contractVersion
  - draft.contractMode
  - draft.contractHash
  - payment
- Activation service responsibilities:
  - validate draft has canonical contract metadata
  - derive startDate from contractSnapshot.start.resolvedStartDate
  - derive plan dimensions from contractSnapshot.plan
  - derive pricing metadata from contractSnapshot.pricing
  - copy canonical contract fields from draft to subscription
  - preserve existing legacy runtime-compatible fields on subscription:
    - selectedGrams
    - selectedMealsPerDay
    - basePlanPriceHalala
    - checkoutCurrency
    - delivery fields
    - current premium/add-on balance rows from draft
  - create day rows based on canonical daysCount
- In [subscriptionController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js):
  - finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment(...) should decide:
    - canonical draft + flag on => activation service
    - otherwise => current legacy inline activation logic

8. **What legacy paths remain untouched**
- Webhook/manual verify entrypoints remain untouched.
- Admin-created subscription runtime remains untouched.
- Admin create does not start writing canonical contracts yet.
- Existing legacy checkout drafts remain valid and continue to activate through current logic.
- Premium behavior remains unchanged.
- Add-on behavior remains unchanged.
- Delivery behavior remains flat/settings-based.
- Planning behavior remains unchanged.
- Existing checkout response payloads should remain unchanged.

9. **Risks in Slice B**
- The biggest risk is partial divergence between top-level draft fields and contractSnapshot if both are persisted but not kept aligned.
- finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment(...) is already used outside the direct customer verify flow, so changing its internals can indirectly affect admin verification of checkout drafts even if we do not touch admin entrypoints.
- If the write flag is enabled but activation flag is off, there can be a coexistence period where canonical draft metadata exists but is not yet used.
- Omitted startDate = tomorrow becomes a real customer behavior change for new canonical drafts.
- Activation from snapshot must preserve all current legacy-compatible subscription fields or later flows may break silently.
- There is some risk of hidden date drift if snapshot start dates and legacy draft.startDate are not stored consistently.

10. **Test plan for Slice B**
- Checkout draft writing tests:
  - canonical draft fields are written when write flag is on
  - canonical draft fields are absent when write flag is off
  - existing checkout response shape stays unchanged
  - legacy requestHash and idempotent reuse behavior still work
  - omitted startDate produces tomorrow in the stored canonical contract
- Activation service tests:
  - canonical draft activates into subscription with contract fields copied over
  - day rows are created from snapshot daysCount
  - subscription uses snapshot start date
  - pricing/base-plan metadata comes from snapshot
  - premium/add-on legacy runtime fields are still populated from draft as before
- Finalization routing tests:
  - canonical draft + activation flag on => activation service path
  - legacy draft => legacy activation path
  - canonical draft + activation flag off => legacy activation path
- Regression tests:
  - existing legacy draft payment finalization still works unchanged
  - no webhook behavior changes
  - no admin-created subscription behavior changes
- Date tests:
  - omitted startDate on new canonical checkout results in tomorrow-based subscription activation
  - explicit future startDate remains honored

11. **Anything ambiguous that still needs explicit approval before coding**
- For canonical customer drafts, should top-level CheckoutDraft.startDate also be written as the resolved tomorrow/future date immediately?
  - I recommend yes, to avoid divergence between legacy fields and contractSnapshot.
- When snapshot activation is enabled, should finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment(...) copy contractSnapshot to Subscription exactly as stored on the draft, or should it append activation-time metadata?
  - I recommend copying it as stored, without mutating the business contract in Slice B.
- Should the write flag and activation flag be allowed to roll out independently, or do you want them enabled together in production?
  - I recommend independent rollout for safety.

ده الرد 
1. **Flag safety review**
- When both flags are off:
  - checkoutSubscription behaves exactly as before for runtime purposes.
  - No canonical contract fields are written to new drafts.
  - finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment always uses the legacy inline activation path.
- When only PHASE1_CANONICAL_CHECKOUT_DRAFT_WRITE=true:
  - New customer checkout drafts get canonical contract fields.
  - CheckoutDraft.startDate is written from the same resolved canonical start date.
  - Activation still uses the legacy path, because PHASE1_CANONICAL_DRAFT_ACTIVATION is off.
  - This means omitted startDate becomes “tomorrow in KSA” for those new canonical drafts, even though activation is still legacy, because legacy activation reads draft.startDate.
- When only PHASE1_CANONICAL_DRAFT_ACTIVATION=true:
  - New checkouts still create legacy drafts because canonical draft writing is off.
  - Legacy drafts do not switch to canonical activation.
  - Only already-canonical drafts, if any exist, would activate through the shared snapshot path.
- There is no accidental activation-path switch for legacy drafts.
  - The gate is explicitly:
    - activation flag enabled
    - and isCanonicalCheckoutDraft(draft) === true
  - If either condition fails, the old activation code runs.

2. **Activation parity review**
- Canonical activation still populates the same legacy-compatible subscription fields as the old path:
  - userId
  - planId
  - status
  - startDate
  - endDate
  - validityEndDate
  - totalMeals
  - remainingMeals
  - premiumRemaining
  - selectedGrams
  - selectedMealsPerDay
  - basePlanPriceHalala
  - checkoutCurrency
  - premiumBalance
  - addonBalance
  - addonSubscriptions
  - deliveryMode
  - deliveryAddress
  - deliveryWindow
  - deliverySlot
- Canonical activation also adds the new contract fields onto Subscription:
  - contractVersion
  - contractMode
  - contractCompleteness
  - contractSource
  - contractHash
  - contractSnapshot
  - renewedFromSubscriptionId
- SubscriptionDay creation matches the legacy path in structure:
  - one row per day
  - date generated with toKSADateString(addDays(start, i))
  - status: "open"
  - only inserts if no existing day rows exist
- Possible divergence points between legacy activation and canonical activation:
  - Canonical activation uses snapshot.plan, snapshot.pricing, and snapshot.delivery, while legacy activation uses top-level draft fields.
  - For normal customer canonical drafts these should align, but if draft top-level fields and snapshot are manually corrupted, canonical path will prefer snapshot-derived values for most business fields.
  - planId currently prefers draft.planId first, then falls back to snapshot.plan.planId. In practice they should match, but this is one possible divergence point if data is inconsistent.
  - pricing.vatPercentage in the snapshot currently depends on what resolvedQuote.breakdown contains. The live quote path does not appear to populate vatPercentage, so snapshot pricing.vatPercentage may currently be 0 even while vatHalala is correct. This does not break activation today, but it is a data-quality gap to keep in mind.

3. **Finalization path review**
- finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment now decides like this:
  - if draft missing: return unchanged error result
  - if user mismatch: return unchanged error result
  - if draft already has a subscription: reuse completion path unchanged
  - if draft status is not recoverable: return unchanged error result
  - if activation flag is on and draft is canonical: call activateSubscriptionFromCanonicalDraft(...)
  - otherwise: run the existing legacy inline activation logic
- Non-customer or indirectly reused paths that can be affected:
  - user checkout verification path in [subscriptionController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js)
  - admin payment-side-effects path in [adminController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js), because it also calls finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment(...) for subscription_activation payments with draftId
- Admin-created subscription runtime itself is still untouched.
- Payment-applied semantics remain unchanged.
  - payment.applied claiming still happens outside finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment
  - Slice B only changes how the subscription gets created after the payment has already been claimed for application

4. **Draft consistency review**
- For canonical customer drafts, top-level CheckoutDraft and contractSnapshot are aligned for:
  - startDate
  - planId / plan.planId
  - daysCount
  - grams / plan.selectedGrams
  - mealsPerDay / plan.mealsPerDay
  - delivery
  - premiumItems
  - addonItems
  - addonSubscriptions
  - breakdown / pricing
- The most important alignment improvement is confirmed:
  - top-level CheckoutDraft.startDate now uses the same resolved canonical start date
- Remaining possible divergence points:
  - requestHash is still computed from the legacy checkout quote shape, not from the canonical contract
  - breakdown does not carry vatPercentage, while contractSnapshot.pricing does
  - planId top-level is an ObjectId, while contractSnapshot.plan.planId is a string representation
  - if any future code mutates top-level draft fields after creation, the snapshot will not auto-update
- In the current Slice B code, no known live path mutates draft fields after creation before payment finalization.

5. **Test review**
- Slice B tests added:
  - buildCanonicalDraftPersistenceFields keeps top-level draft startDate aligned with canonical contract
  - isCanonicalCheckoutDraft identifies authoritative canonical drafts
  - buildCanonicalSubscriptionActivationPayload copies canonical contract metadata and legacy runtime fields
  - activateSubscriptionFromCanonicalDraft persists subscription, days, and completion state
- Important behaviors still untested:
  - controller-level test for checkoutSubscription with draft-write flag on
  - controller-level test for checkoutSubscription with both flags off
  - controller-level or service-branch test for finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment choosing canonical vs legacy activation
  - regression test proving legacy drafts stay on legacy activation even when activation flag is on
  - indirect admin path regression for canonical checkout drafts
  - response-shape regression for checkout initiation
- Yes, one integration-style regression test would still be useful before merge or before enabling flags:
  - ideally a test around checkoutSubscription draft creation under the write flag
  - and a test around finalizeSubscriptionDraftPayment branch selection for canonical vs legacy drafts

6. **Ready-for-merge assessment**
- safe to merge with minor follow-up

- Briefly why:
  - The flags default off, so the new behavior is dark by default.
  - Legacy drafts and legacy subscriptions remain supported.
  - The main follow-up I’d still want is a small integration-style regression around controller-path branching before enabling the flags in any real environment.

1. **Scope of Slice C**
- Implement P1-W06, P1-W07, and P1-W08 only.
- Move admin-created subscriptions onto the Phase 1 canonical contract path.
- Introduce one shared payment side-effect dispatcher for the existing Phase 1 payment types.
- Make these three entrypoints converge on that shared apply path after payment status reconciliation and claim:
  - customer manual verify in [subscriptionController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js)
  - admin verify in [adminController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js)
  - webhook processing in [webhookController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js)
- Keep Slice C narrow:
  - no premium redesign
  - no add-on redesign
  - no delivery redesign
  - no planning redesign
  - no legacy removal

2. **Exact behavior changes introduced by Slice C**
- Admin-created subscriptions will start using the same canonical contract builder as customer checkout.
- Admin-created subscriptions will use the same snapshot-based activation service as canonical checkout subscriptions.
- Omitted startDate for admin-created subscriptions will resolve to tomorrow in KSA once the canonical admin-create path is enabled.
- Payment side effects for supported Phase 1 payment types will be applied by one shared dispatcher instead of duplicated logic across admin verify and webhook, and partly separate logic in customer manual verify.
- Provider status reconciliation, mismatch checks, and claim semantics stay local to each entrypoint; only side-effect application converges.
- Existing business semantics of each supported payment type remain unchanged.

3. **Exact files likely to change**
- [adminController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/adminController.js)
- [subscriptionController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/subscriptionController.js)
- [webhookController.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/controllers/webhookController.js)
- [subscriptionActivationService.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/subscriptionActivationService.js)
- [subscriptionContractService.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/services/subscriptionContractService.js)
- [featureFlags.js](/home/hema/Projects/basicdiet145/src/utils/featureFlags.js)

Likely new file:
- src/services/paymentApplicationService.js

Likely tests:
- test/paymentApplicationService.test.js
- test/adminCanonicalCreate.test.js
- updates to Slice B/verify-related tests or a new test/verifyConvergence.test.js

4. **New modules/services to create or extend**
- Create paymentApplicationService.js
  - recommended public entry:
    - applyPaymentSideEffects({ payment, session, source })
  - recommended internal handlers:
    - applySubscriptionActivationPayment(...)
    - applyWalletTopupPayment(...)
    - applyOneTimeAddonPayment(...)
    - applyCustomSaladDayPayment(...)
    - applyCustomMealDayPayment(...)
- Extend subscriptionActivationService.js
  - add a contract-based activation path for admin-created subscriptions, so admin create does not need to fake a checkout draft
  - recommended public entry:
    - activateSubscriptionFromCanonicalContract({ userId, planId, contract, legacyRuntimeData, session })
- Extend subscriptionContractService.js
  - only if needed for admin-specific origin metadata or admin override metadata normalization
- Extend featureFlags.js
  - add Slice C flags

5. **How admin-created subscriptions will align with the canonical contract**
- createSubscriptionAdmin(...) should still resolve a quote first.
- Then, when the Slice C admin canonical flag is enabled:
  - build a Phase 1 canonical contract with:
    - source: "admin_create"
    - actorRole: "admin"
    - actorUserId: req.dashboardUserId
    - adminOverrideMeta if needed
  - activate using the shared canonical activation service
- The created Subscription should store:
  - the same Phase 1 contract fields as customer-created canonical subscriptions
- Admin-specific runtime notes:
  - it still becomes active immediately, as today
  - no payment flow is introduced for admin create
  - no premium/add-on semantics are redesigned
- This gives admin-created subscriptions the same contract foundation without changing their business intent.

6. **How the shared payment application dispatcher will work**
- Each caller still does its own:
  - provider fetch or provider payload read
  - amount/currency/id mismatch checks
  - transaction start
  - payment.applied claim
- After a payment is claimed, the caller invokes:
  - applyPaymentSideEffects({ payment: claimedPayment, session, source })
- The dispatcher determines behavior only from stored payment.type and stored payment.metadata
- It returns a normalized result:
  - applied: true/false
  - reason
  - optional subscriptionId, dayId, or similar identifiers
- The dispatcher must preserve current semantics:
  - if side effects cannot be applied, the caller can still write unappliedReason exactly as today
- The dispatcher should support both:
  - checkout-draft subscription activation
  - legacy subscriptionId activation path for old initiated payments

7. **How webhook verify, manual verify, and admin verify will converge**
- They will converge only at the “apply side effects” stage.
- They will not be unified into one controller flow.
- Recommended convergence model:
  - verifyCheckoutDraftPayment(...)
    - after claim, call shared dispatcher
  - verifyPaymentAdmin(...)
    - replace applyAdminPaymentSideEffects(...) with shared dispatcher
  - handleMoyasarWebhook(...)
    - replace the large in-controller payment-type switch with shared dispatcher
- Non-paid terminal handling can stay local for Slice C if needed, especially where current behavior differs slightly by entrypoint.
- This keeps migration risk lower while still removing the biggest duplication: paid side-effect application.

8. **What payment types remain supported in the shared dispatcher in Phase 1**
Recommended supported types in Slice C:
- subscription_activation
  - checkout draft path via metadata.draftId
  - legacy pending-subscription path via metadata.subscriptionId
- premium_topup
- addon_topup
- one_time_addon
- custom_salad_day
- custom_meal_day

Recommended to keep out of Slice C for now:
- one_time_order
  - it is not part of the subscription Phase 1 scope
  - it currently exists only in webhook logic and can remain untouched for now

9. **What paths remain untouched in Slice C**
- Checkout draft creation path from Slice B
- Slice A contract/idempotency scaffolding
- Premium runtime semantics
- Add-on runtime semantics
- Delivery runtime semantics
- Planning runtime semantics
- Freeze/skip runtime semantics
- Legacy draft support
- Legacy subscription support
- Order payment flows, especially one_time_order, unless explicitly approved to include

10. **Risks in Slice C**
- The biggest risk is converging duplicated payment side effects without changing subtle behavior differences by accident.
- adminController.verifyPaymentAdmin and webhookController.handleMoyasarWebhook currently have overlapping but not identical logic, so the dispatcher must be source-of-truth only for application, not for provider reconciliation.
- Admin-created subscriptions will become canonical and tomorrow-default when the admin canonical flag is enabled; this is a real admin-facing behavior change.
- There is a legacy subscription_activation path by metadata.subscriptionId that must remain supported.
- If dispatcher ownership is unclear, there is risk of circular dependencies between controllers and services.

11. **Test plan for Slice C**
- Admin canonical create tests:
  - admin create with flag off => legacy path unchanged
  - admin create with flag on => canonical contract written to subscription
  - omitted startDate on admin canonical create => tomorrow in KSA
  - admin create response remains backward-compatible
- Payment dispatcher tests:
  - each supported payment type applies the same business effect as before
  - unsupported types return applied: false with stable reasons
  - legacy subscription_activation by subscriptionId still works
- Convergence tests:
  - manual verify uses dispatcher after claim
  - admin verify uses dispatcher after claim
  - webhook uses dispatcher after claim
  - payment.applied semantics remain unchanged
  - unappliedReason behavior remains unchanged
- Regression tests:
  - legacy drafts still finalize correctly
  - legacy subscriptions still activate correctly
  - one_time_order remains untouched
- Suggested rollout tests:
  - flag-off behavior regression
  - flag-on canary behavior for admin create
  - flag-on dispatcher behavior for each supported payment type

12. **Anything ambiguous that still needs explicit approval before coding**
- Should one_time_order stay out of Slice C and remain untouched for now?
  - I recommend yes, to keep Slice C strictly within the approved subscription scope.
- Should admin-created canonical subscriptions be behind a dedicated flag independent from the shared payment dispatcher flag?
  - I recommend yes, for safer rollout.
- Should admin API responses start exposing richer canonical metadata immediately when the admin canonical path is enabled, or should Slice C keep response changes minimal and only store the metadata?
  - I recommend minimal response changes in Slice C, with richer admin exposure deferred unless you want it now.

ده االرد 
1. **Flag safety review**
- When both new Slice C flags are off:
  - PHASE1_CANONICAL_ADMIN_CREATE=false
  - PHASE1_SHARED_PAYMENT_DISPATCHER=false
  - admin-created subscriptions stay fully on the legacy create path
  - customer manual verify stays on legacy apply logic
  - admin verify stays on legacy applyAdminPaymentSideEffects(...)
  - webhook stays on its old in-controller switch logic
  - this is safe and unchanged

- When only PHASE1_CANONICAL_ADMIN_CREATE is on:
  - admin-created subscriptions use the canonical contract builder and canonical activation service
  - webhook/manual/admin payment verification paths remain legacy
  - no dispatcher behavior changes occur
  - this is isolated and behaves as intended

- When only PHASE1_SHARED_PAYMENT_DISPATCHER is on:
  - admin-created subscriptions remain legacy
  - customer manual verify, admin verify, and webhook can route supported payment types through the shared dispatcher
  - legacy checkout/admin create behavior remains intact
  - this is mostly correct, but there is one important caveat:
    - webhook checks the supported-type set before using the dispatcher
    - admin verify currently does not pre-filter unsupported types before calling the dispatcher
    - so unsupported payment types do not fall back safely in every path yet

- Confirm unsupported payment types still fall back safely:
  - webhook: yes
  - customer manual verify: effectively yes for current covered endpoints, because those endpoints only deal with supported payment types
  - admin verify: not fully
  - important finding: if PHASE1_SHARED_PAYMENT_DISPATCHER=true and admin verifies an unsupported type such as one_time_order, it will hit the dispatcher instead of falling back to legacy admin logic

2. **Dispatcher parity review**
- subscription_activation
  - handled by applySubscriptionActivationPayment(...)
  - if metadata.draftId exists, it loads the draft and calls the shared draft finalization flow
  - if metadata.subscriptionId exists, it activates the pending legacy subscription path
  - semantics are intended to remain unchanged

- premium_topup
  - handled by applyPremiumTopupPayment(...)
  - loads the subscription and appends premium wallet rows from payment metadata
  - preserves legacy premium sync helpers
  - semantics remain aligned with the old top-up path

- addon_topup
  - handled by applyAddonTopupPayment(...)
  - loads the subscription and appends add-on wallet rows from payment metadata
  - semantics remain aligned with the old add-on top-up path

- one_time_addon
  - handled by applyOneTimeAddonPayment(...)
  - adds the paid add-on to the target day only if the day is open
  - semantics remain aligned with the old path

- custom_salad_day
  - handled by applyCustomSaladDayPayment(...)
  - creates or updates the day-level custom salad payload if the day is open
  - semantics remain aligned with the old path

- custom_meal_day
  - handled by applyCustomMealDayPayment(...)
  - creates or updates the day-level custom meal payload if the day is open
  - semantics remain aligned with the old path

- Confirm current business semantics remain unchanged:
  - broadly yes for the supported set
  - the dispatcher preserves the existing meanings of those payment types

- Payment type behavior that may still differ subtly from old paths:
  - admin verify unsupported-type fallback is incomplete, especially for one_time_order
  - webhook support filtering is explicit, but admin verify is currently broader than intended
  - manual top-up verify now routes through the dispatcher when flagged, which reloads the subscription inside the service rather than reusing an already-loaded in-session reference; semantics should match, but it is still a path difference

3. **Verify-path convergence review**
- Customer manual verify:
  - still performs provider reconciliation locally
  - still performs amount/currency/id checks locally
  - still claims payment.applied locally
  - then chooses:
    - dispatcher if PHASE1_SHARED_PAYMENT_DISPATCHER=true
    - legacy apply logic otherwise

- Admin verify:
  - still performs provider reconciliation locally
  - still performs amount/currency/id checks locally
  - still claims payment.applied locally
  - then chooses:
    - dispatcher if PHASE1_SHARED_PAYMENT_DISPATCHER=true
    - legacy applyAdminPaymentSideEffects(...) otherwise
  - this is where the unsupported-type issue exists

- Webhook:
  - still performs payment lookup, mismatch checks, and status updates locally
  - still claims payment.applied locally
  - then chooses:
    - dispatcher only if the flag is on and the payment type is in the supported set
    - legacy switch otherwise

- Confirm provider reconciliation and claim semantics remain local and unchanged:
  - yes

- Confirm payment.applied and unappliedReason behavior remain unchanged:
  - mostly yes
  - the claim/update pattern remains the same
  - unappliedReason handling is still present
  - the one caveat is that an unsupported admin-verified payment under dispatcher flag would now produce dispatcher-style unsupported behavior instead of legacy side effects

4. **Admin canonical-create review**
- Legacy-compatible subscription fields still populated by canonical admin create:
  - userId
  - planId
  - status
  - startDate
  - endDate
  - validityEndDate
  - totalMeals
  - remainingMeals
  - premiumRemaining
  - selectedGrams
  - selectedMealsPerDay
  - basePlanPriceHalala
  - checkoutCurrency
  - premiumBalance
  - addonBalance
  - addonSubscriptions
  - deliveryMode
  - deliveryAddress
  - deliveryWindow
  - deliverySlot
  - plus the new canonical contract metadata fields

- Confirm admin response shape remains minimal:
  - yes
  - it still returns the normal serialized admin subscription payload plus existing meta style
  - no broad admin response expansion was introduced

- Possible divergence between legacy admin create and canonical admin create:
  - omitted startDate now resolves to tomorrow in KSA when canonical admin-create flag is on
  - legacy admin create previously defaulted effectively to “now/today”
  - canonical admin create stores contract metadata while legacy does not
  - canonical admin create derives values from the canonical contract plus passed legacy-runtime data rather than inline quote fields, though it is intended to align

5. **Test review**
- Slice C tests added:
  - paymentApplicationService.test.js
    - supported payment type set
    - subscription activation via draft path
    - legacy subscription activation via subscriptionId
    - premium top-up application
    - one-time add-on application
    - explicit exclusion of one_time_order
  - adminCanonicalCreate.test.js
    - canonical admin-create path behind flag
    - canonical contract builder usage
    - canonical activation service usage
    - minimal response behavior retained

- Important controller/integration behaviors still untested:
  - verifyCheckoutDraftPayment branch selection: dispatcher vs legacy
  - verifyWalletTopupPayment branch selection: dispatcher vs legacy
  - verifyPaymentAdmin branch selection: dispatcher vs legacy
  - handleMoyasarWebhook branch selection for supported vs unsupported types
  - explicit regression for unsupported admin-verified payment types when dispatcher flag is on
  - explicit admin-create legacy-path regression when the admin canonical flag is off

- Additional regression test recommended before merge or before enabling flags:
  - yes
  - at minimum, add a controller-style regression around verifyPaymentAdmin with PHASE1_SHARED_PAYMENT_DISPATCHER=true and an unsupported type like one_time_order
  - also recommended: one webhook branch-selection regression and one manual verify branch-selection regression

6. **Ready-for-merge assessment**
- not safe to merge yet

- Briefly:
  - default-off behavior is safe, and most Slice C work is correctly isolated
  - but unsupported payment types do not fall back safely in all verify paths yet, specifically admin verify when the shared dispatcher flag is enabled
  - that conflicts with the approved Slice C boundary and should be fixed or explicitly gated before calling Slice C merge-ready
